# Searching Sourcegraph

Search before you build. Existing patterns reduce tokens, ensure consistency, and surface tested solutions.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Tool Selection Logic

**Start here:**

1. **Know the exact symbol or pattern?** → `sg_keyword_search`
2. **Know the concept, not the code?** → `sg_nls_search`
3. **Need to understand how/why?** → `sg_deepsearch_read`
4. **Tracing a symbol's usage?** → `sg_find_references`
5. **Need full implementation?** → `sg_go_to_definition` → `sg_read_file`

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Exact code patterns | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Trace usage | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Understand systems | `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Read files | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
file:.*\.test\.ts$ -file:__mocks__   # Tests, exclude mocks
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

Combine filters: `repo:^github.com/myorg/backend$ file:src/handlers lang:typescript`

## Context-Aware Behaviour

**When the user provides a file path or error message:**
- Extract symbols, function names, or error codes
- Search for those exact terms first
- Trace references if the error involves a known symbol

**When the user asks "how does X work":**
- Prefer `sg_deepsearch_read` for architectural understanding
- Follow up with `sg_read_file` on key files mentioned in the response

**When the user is implementing a new feature:**
- Search for similar existing implementations first
- Read tests for usage examples
- Check for shared utilities before creating new ones

**When debugging:**
- Search for the exact error string
- Trace the symbol where the error is thrown
- Check recent changes with `sg_diff_search`

## Workflows

For detailed step-by-step workflows, see:
- `workflows/implementing-feature.md` — when building new features
- `workflows/understanding-code.md` — when exploring unfamiliar systems
- `workflows/debugging-issue.md` — when tracking down bugs

## Efficiency Rules

**Minimise tool calls:**
- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms (faster, more precise)

**Batch your understanding:**
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than reading one and asking questions
- Use `sg_deepsearch_read` for "how does X work" instead of multiple keyword searches

**Avoid common token waste:**
- Don't search all repos when you know the target repo
- Don't use `sg_deepsearch_read` for simple "find all" queries
- Don't re-read files you've already seen in this conversation

## Query Patterns

| Intent | Query |
|--------|-------|
| React hooks | `file:.*\.tsx$ use[A-Z].*= \(` |
| API routes | `file:src/api app\.(get\|post\|put\|delete)` |
| Error handling | `catch.*Error\|\.catch\(` |
| Type definitions | `file:types/ export (interface\|type)` |
| Test setup | `file:.*\.test\. beforeEach\|beforeAll` |
| Config files | `file:(webpack\|vite\|rollup)\.config` |
| CI/CD | `file:\.github/workflows deploy` |

For more patterns, see `query-patterns.md`.

## Output Formatting

**Search results:**
- Present as a brief summary, not raw tool output
- Highlight the most relevant file and line
- Include a code snippet only if it directly answers the question

**Code explanations:**
- Start with a one-sentence summary
- Use the codebase's own terminology
- Reference specific files and functions

**Recommendations:**
- Present as numbered steps if actionable
- Link to specific patterns found in the codebase
- Note any existing utilities that should be reused

## Common Mistakes

| Mistake | Fix |
|---------|-----|
| Searching all repos | Add `repo:^github.com/org/repo$` |
| Too many results | Add `file:` pattern or keywords |
| Missing relevant code | Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching |
| Not understanding context | Use `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Guessing patterns | Read implementations with `sg_read_file` |

## Principles

- Start narrow, expand if needed
- Chain tools: search → read → find references → definition
- Check tests for usage examples
- Read before generating

**Repository:** kubernetes/kubernetes (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce an algorithmic deep-dive on APF QueueSet behavior, dispatch flow, and fairness tradeoffs.

## Scope

Focus on the APF QueueSet subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

// QueueSetFactory is used to create QueueSet objects.  Creation, like
// config update, is done in two phases: the first phase consumes the
// QueuingConfig and the second consumes the DispatchingConfig.  They
// are separated so that errors from the first phase can be found
// before committing to a concurrency allotment for the second.
type QueueSetFactory interface {
	// BeginConstruction does the first phase of creating a QueueSet.
	// The RatioedGaugePair observes number of requests,
	// execution covering just the regular phase.
	// The denominator for the waiting phase is
	// max(1, QueuingConfig.QueueLengthLimit) X max(1, QueuingConfig.DesiredNumQueues).
	// The RatioedGauge observes number of seats occupied through all phases of execution.
	// The denominator for all the ratioed concurrency gauges is supplied later in the DispatchingConfig.
	// The Gauge observes the seat demand (executing + queued seats).
	BeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, metrics.RatioedGaugePair, metrics.RatioedGauge, metrics.Gauge) (QueueSetCom
... (truncated)

package queueset

import (
	"container/list"

// removeFromFIFOFunc removes a designated element from the list
// if that element is in the list.
// The complexity of the runtime cost is O(1).
// The returned value is the element removed, if indeed one was removed,
// otherwise `nil`.
type removeFromFIFOFunc func() *request

// walkFunc is called for each request in the list in the
// oldest -> newest order.
// ok: if walkFunc returns false then the iteration stops immediately.
// walkFunc may remove the given request from the fifo,
// but may not mutate the fifo in any othe way.
type walkFunc func(*request) (ok bool)

// Internal interface to abstract out the implementation details
// of the underlying list used to maintain the requests.
//
// Note that a fifo, including the removeFromFIFOFuncs returned from Enqueue,
// is not safe for concurrent use by multiple goroutines.
type fifo interface {
	// Enqueue enqueues the specified request into the list and
	// returns a removeFromFIFOFunc function that can be used to remove the
	// request from the list
	Enqueue(*request) removeFromFIFOFunc

	// Dequeue pulls out the oldest request from the list.
	Dequeue() (*request, bool)

	// Peek returns the oldest reque

// WorkEstimate carries three of the four parameters that determine the work in a request.
// The fourth parameter is the duration of the initial phase of execution.
type WorkEstimate struct {
	// InitialSeats is the number of seats occupied while the server is
	// executing this request.
	InitialSeats uint64

	// FinalSeats is the number of seats occupied at the end,
	// during the AdditionalLatency.
	FinalSeats uint64

	// AdditionalLatency specifies the additional duration the seats allocated
	// to this request must be reserved after the given request had finished.
	// AdditionalLatency should not have any impact on the user experience, the
	// caller must not experience this additional latency.
	AdditionalLatency time.Duration
}

// MaxSeats returns the maximum number of seats the request occupies over the
// phases of being served.
func (we *WorkEstimate) MaxSeats() int {
	if we.InitialSeats >= we.FinalSeats {
		return int(we.InitialSeats)
	}

	return int(we.FinalSe
... (truncated)

package promise

import (
	"context"
	"sync"
)

// promise implements the WriteOnce interface.
type promise struct {
	doneCtx context.Context
	doneVal interface{}
	setCh   chan struct{}
	onceler sync.Once
	value   interface{}
}

var _ WriteOnce = &promise{}

// NewWriteOnce makes a new thread-safe WriteOnce.
//
// If `initial` is non-nil then that value is Set at creation time.
//
// If a `Get` is waiting soon after the channel associated with the
// `doneCtx` becomes selectable (which never happens for the nil
// channel) then `Set(doneVal)` effectively happens at that time.
func NewWriteOnce(initial interface{}, doneCtx context.Context, doneVal interface{}) WriteOnce {
	p := &promise{
		doneCtx: doneCtx,
		doneVal: doneVal,
		setCh:   make(chan struct{}),
	}
	if initial != nil {
		p.Set(initial)
	}
	return p
}

func (p *promise) Get() interface{} {
	select {
	case <-p.setCh:
	case <-p.doneCtx.Done():
		p.Set(p.doneVal)
	}
	return p.value
}

func (p *promise) Set(value interface{}) bool {
	var ans bool
	p.onceler.Do(func() {
		p.value = value
		close(p.setCh)
		ans = true
	})
	return ans
}

// Integrator computes the moments of some variable X over time as
// read from a particular clock.  The integrals start when the
// Integrator is created, and ends at the latest operation on the
// Integrator.
type Integrator interface {
	fcmetrics.Gauge

	GetResults() IntegratorResults

	// Return the results of integrating to now, and reset integration to start now
	Reset() IntegratorResults
}

// IntegratorResults holds statistical abstracts of the integration
type IntegratorResults struct {
	Duration  float64 //seconds
	Average   float64 //time-weighted
	Deviation float64 //standard deviation: sqrt(avg((value-avg)^2))
	Min, Max  float64
}

// Equal tests for semantic equality.
// This considers all NaN values to be equal to each other.
func (x *IntegratorResults) Equal(y *IntegratorResults) bool {
	return x == y || x != nil && y != nil && x.Duration == y.Duration && x.Min == y.Min && x.Max == y.Max && (x.Average == y.Average || math.IsNaN(x.Average) && math.IsNaN(y.Average)) && (x.Deviation == y.Deviation || math.IsNaN(x.Deviation) && math.IsNaN(y.Deviation))
}

package shufflesharding

import (
	"fmt"
	"math"
)

// MaxHashBits is the max bit length which can be used from hash value.
// If we use all bits of hash value, the critical(last) card shuffled by
// Dealer will be uneven to 2:3 (first half:second half) at most,
// in order to reduce this unevenness to 32:33, we set MaxHashBits to 60 here.
const MaxHashBits = 60

// RequiredEntropyBits makes a quick and slightly conservative estimate of the number
// of bits of hash value that are consumed in shuffle sharding a deck of the given size
// to a hand of the given size.  The result is meaningful only if
// 1 <= handSize <= deckSize <= 1<<26.
func RequiredEntropyBits(deckSize, handSize int) int {
	return int(math.Ceil(math.Log2(float64(deckSize)) * float64(handSize)))
}

// Dealer contains some necessary parameters and provides some methods for shuffle sharding.
// Dealer is thread-safe.
type Dealer struct {
	deckSize int
	handSize int
}

// NewDealer will create a Dealer with the given deckSize and handSize, will return error when
// deckSize or handSize is invalid as below.
// 1. deckSize or handSize is not positive
// 2. handSize is greater than deckSize
// 3. deckSize is impractically large (greater than 1<<26)

... (truncated)

		return nil, nil

	if err != nil {
		err = fmt.Errorf("the QueueSetConfig implies an invalid shuffle sharding config (DesiredNumQueues is deckSize): %w", err)
	}
	return dealer, err
}

func (qsc *queueSetCompleter) Complete(dCfg fq.DispatchingConfig) fq.QueueSet {
	qs := qsc.theSet
	if qs == nil {
		qs = &queueSet{
			clock:                    qsc.factory.clock,
			estimatedServiceDuration: 3 * time.Millisecond,
			reqsGaugePair:            qsc.reqsGaugePair,
			execSeatsGauge:           qsc.execSeatsGauge,
			seatDemandIntegrator:     qsc.seatDemandIntegrator,
			qCfg:                     qsc.qCfg,
			currentR:                 0,
			lastRealTime:             qsc.factory.clock.Now(),
			requestsExecutingSet:     sets.New[*request](),
		}
		qs.promiseFactory = qsc.factory.promiseFactoryFactory(qs)
	}
	qs.setConfiguration(context.Background(), qsc.qCfg, qsc.dealer, dCfg)
	return qs
}

// createQueues is a helper method for initializing an array of n queues
func createQueues(n, baseIndex int) []*queue {
	fqqueues := make([]*queue, n)
	for i := 0; i < n; i++ {
		fqqueues[i] = &queue{index: baseIndex + i, requestsWaiting: newRequestFIFO(), requestsExecuting: sets.New[*request]()}
	}
	return fqqueues
}

func (qs *queueSet) BeginConfigChange(qCfg fq.QueuingConfig) (fq.QueueSetCompleter, error) {
	dealer, err := checkConfig(qCfg)
	if err != nil {
		return nil, err
	}
	return &queueSetCompleter{
		theSet: qs,
		qCfg:   qCfg,
		dealer: dealer}, nil
}

			// It is safe to reset to zero in this case, because the next request
			// will overwrite the zero with `qs.currentR`.
			queue.nextDispatchR = 0
			continue
		}
		oldNextDispatchR := queue.nextDispatchR
		queue.nextDispatchR -= rDecrement
		if queue.nextDispatchR > oldNextDispatchR {
			klog.ErrorS(errors.New("queue::nextDispatchR underflow"), "Underflow", "QS", qs.qCfg.Name, "queue", qIdx, "oldNextDispatchR", oldNextDispatchR, "newNextDispatchR", queue.nextDispatchR, "incrR", incrR)
			success = false
		}
		queue.requestsWaiting.Walk(func(req *request) bool {
			oldArrivalR := req.arrivalR
			req.arrivalR -= rDecrement
			if req.arrivalR > oldArrivalR {
				klog.ErrorS(errors.New("request::arrivalR underflow"), "Underflow", "QS", qs.qCfg.Name, "queue", qIdx, "request", *req, "oldArrivalR", oldArrivalR, "incrR", incrR)
				success = false
			}
			return true
		})
	}
	metrics.AddEpochAdvance(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, success)
}

// getVirtualTimeRatio calculates the rate at which virtual time has
// been advancing, according to the logic in `doc.go`.
func (qs *queueSet) getVirtualTimeRatioLocked() float64 {
	activeQueues := 0
	seatsRequested := 0
	for _, queue := range qs.queues {
		// here we want the sum of the maximum width of the requests in this queue since our
		// goal is to find the maximum rate at which the queue could work.
		seatsRequested += (queue.seatsInUse + queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum().MaxSeatsSum)
		if queue.requestsWaiting.Length() > 0 || queue.requestsExecuting.Len() > 0 {
			activeQueues++
		}
	}
	if activeQueues == 0 {
		return 0
	}
	return math.Min(float64(seatsRequested), float64(qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit)) / float64(activeQueues)
}

// QueueSetFactory is used to create QueueSet objects.  Creation, like
// config update, is done in two phases: the first phase consumes the
// QueuingConfig and the second consumes the DispatchingConfig.  They
// are separated so that errors from the first phase can be found
// before committing to a concurrency allotment for the second.
type QueueSetFactory interface {
	// BeginConstruction does the first phase of creating a QueueSet.
	// The RatioedGaugePair observes number of requests,
	// execution covering just the regular phase.
	// The denominator for the waiting phase is
	// max(1, QueuingConfig.QueueLengthLimit) X max(1, QueuingConfig.DesiredNumQueues).
	// The RatioedGauge observes number of seats occupied through all phases of execution.
	// The denominator for all the ratioed concurrency gauges is supplied later in the DispatchingConfig.
	// The Gauge observes the seat demand (executing + queued seats).
	BeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, metrics.RatioedGaugePair, metrics.RatioedGauge, metrics.Gauge) (QueueSetCom
... (truncated)

		if klogV.Enabled() {

		}
		metrics.AddDispatchWithNoAccommodation(qs.qCfg.Name, oldestReqFromMinQueue.fsName)
		return nil, nil
	}
	oldestReqFromMinQueue.removeFromQueueLocked()

	// If the requested final seats exceed capacity of that queue,
	// we reduce them to current capacity and adjust additional latency
	// to preserve the total amount of work.
	if oldestReqFromMinQueue.workEstimate.FinalSeats > uint64(qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit) {
		finalSeats := uint64(qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit)
		additionalLatency := oldestReqFromMinQueue.workEstimate.finalWork.DurationPerSeat(float64(finalSeats))
		oldestReqFromMinQueue.workEstimate.FinalSeats = finalSeats
		oldestReqFromMinQueue.workEstimate.AdditionalLatency = additionalLatency
	}

type queueSet struct {
	clock                    eventclock.Interface
	estimatedServiceDuration time.Duration

	reqsGaugePair metrics.RatioedGaugePair // .RequestsExecuting covers regular phase only
	execSeatsGauge metrics.RatioedGauge    // for all phases of execution
	seatDemandIntegrator metrics.Gauge

	promiseFactory promiseFactory

	lock sync.Mutex

	// qCfg holds the current queuing configuration
	qCfg fq.QueuingConfig

	// the current dispatching configuration
	dCfg fq.DispatchingConfig

	// dealer implements shuffle sharding
	dealer *shufflesharding.Dealer

	// queues may be longer than desired while draining
	queues []*queue

	// currentR is the progress meter (virtual time) - seat-seconds allocated per queue since startup
	currentR fqrequest.SeatSeconds

	totSeatsWaiting int
	enqueues int

	totRequestsRejected int

The documentation has been written to `/workspace/documentation.md`. Here is a summary of what it covers:

**Structure (9 sections):**

1. **Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies** — APF sits between auth and the handler chain; QueueSet is the per-priority-level scheduling unit. Upstream (API types, informers, clock) and downstream (handler chain, metrics) dependencies are mapped.

2. **Key Components and Responsibility Split** — Seven components detailed with concrete file paths:
   - `configController` (classification, reconciliation, borrowing)
   - `priorityLevelState` (per-level bookkeeping with concurrency bounds `minCL/maxCL/currentCL`)
   - `queueSet` / `QueueSet` interface (dispatch engine)
   - `queue` (per-queue FIFO + virtual-time pointer `nextDispatchR`)
   - `request` + `WriteOnce` promise (dispatch decision channel)
   - `completedWorkEstimate` (work as seat-seconds)
   - Shuffle sharding `Dealer` (Fisher-Yates queue selection)

3. **End-to-End Request Flow** — Five phases traced through actual function calls: classification (SHA256 hash, FlowSchema matching), queue assignment (shuffle shard → reject-or-enqueue), dispatch loop, blocking wait on promise, and completion with two-phase seat release.

4. **The Fair Queuing Algorithm in Detail** — `currentR` virtual time, WF²Q+ queue selection by minimum virtual finish time, anti-windup hack in `boundNextDispatchLocked`, service-time correction in `finishRequestLocked`, and epoch advance for overflow prevention.

5. **Concurrency Borrowing and Dynamic Limits** — The 10-second rebalance loop, time-weighted integrator, exponential smoothing (`seatDemandSmoothingCoefficient = 0.977`, ~5 min half-life), and the three-case proportional allocation in `updateBorrowingLocked`.

6. **Failure Modes, Limits, an

QUEUESET IMPLEMENTATION DETAILS\n\n#### Architecture Overview\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502                 \u2502\n                 \u25bc\n        \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n        \u2502  APF HTTP Filter   \u2502\n        \u2502  (apf_filter.go)   \u2502\n        \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n                 \u2502\n                 \u251c\u2500\u25ba        \u2502                                                   \u2502\n        \u25bc (if queues disabled)            \u25bc (if queues enabled)\n \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n              \u2502                              \u2502\n              \u2502        \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n              \u2502        \u2502\n              \u25bc        \u25bc\n Dispatch    \u2502\n        \u2502 (Virtual time advance)   \u2502\n        \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n                   \u2502\n                   \u25bc\n        \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n        \u2502 Request.Finish()   \u2502\n        \u2502 (wait for decision)\u2502\n        \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u252c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n                 \u2502\n        \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2534\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n        \u25bc                     \u25bc\n   \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510          \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n   \u2502 Execute \u2502          \u2502  Reject/ \u2502\n   \u2502 Request \u2502          \u2502  Timeout \u2502\n   \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518          \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n#### QueueSet State Machine\n\n**Request States:**\n1. **WAITING**: In queue, awaiting dispatch decision\n2. **EXECUTING**: Running, occupying seats\n3. **FINISHED**: Completed (via execute, reject, or timeout)\n\n**Decision Values:**\n- `decisionExecute`: Allow execution\n- `decisionCancel`: Reject due to timeout/context cancellation\n\n#### Fair Queuing Algorithm (FQSR)\n\n**Virtual Time Concept:**\n- `R` (progress meter): Tracks virtual time in seat-seconds\n- Updated every operation: `R_new = R_old + rate * elapsed_time`\n- Rate based on active queues and concurrency utilization\n\n**Virtual Time Rate Calculation:**\n```\nactiveQueues = count of non-empty queues\nseatsRequested = sum of (executing seats + waiting request max widths)\nrate = min(seatsRequested, concurrencyLimit) / activeQueues\n```\n\n**Per-Queue Dispatch:**\n- `nextDispatchR`: Virtual time at which queue's next request will be dispatched\n- Request `arrivalR`: Virtual time when request was enqueued\n- Queues advance fairness based on work completion\n\n**Shuffle Sharding for Queue Selection:**\n1. Hash request to get random value\n2. Create random \"hand\" of N queue indices (HandSize)\n3. Select queue with minimum pending work among hand\n4. Prevents hash collisions from concentrating load\n\n#### Concurrency Management\n\n**Seat Allocation:**\n- Each request occupies seats during execution\n- `InitialSeats`: Standard concurrency slots\n- `FinalSeats`: Cleanup/write-back phase seats\n- `MaxSeats`: `max(InitialSeats, FinalSeats)` for planning\n\n**Concurrency Limits Per Priority Level:**\n- `nominalCL`: Configured nominal concurrency limit\n- `minCL`: `nominalCL - lendable` (cannot be borrowed away)\n- `maxCL`: `nominalCL + borrowable` (can borrow from others)\n- `currentCL`: Dynamic limit adjusted every 10 seconds\n\n**Borrowing Mechanism (updateBorrowing):**\n- Runs every 10 seconds\n- Tracks seat demand via integrator metrics\n- Adjusts `currentCL` to smooth utilization across priority levels\n- Uses exponential smoothing: `smoothed = 0.977 * smoothed + 0.023 * envelope`\n\n### 4. REQUEST FLOW THROUGH THE SYSTEM\n\n#### Phase 1: Request Arrival & Classification\n\n```go\n// apf_filter.go: Handle()\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502 1. RequestDigest extraction      \u2502 (RequestInfo, User from context)\n\u2502 2. FlowSchema matching           \u2502 (sorted by precedence)\n\u2502 3. Match first applicable schema \u2502\n\u2502 4. Extract PriorityLevelConfig   \u2502\n\u2502 5. Determine flow distinguisher  \u2502 (ByUser, ByNamespace, or empty)\n\u2502 6. Call noteFn callback          \u2502 (metrics update)\n\u2502 7. Hash calculation (SHA256)     \u2502 (from flow distinguisher)\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n#### Phase 2: Work Estimation\n\n```go\n// request/width.go, request/list_work_estimator.go, etc.\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502 workEstimator.estimate()             \u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2524\n\u2502 Verb-based dispatch:                 \u2502\n\u2502  - \"list\" \u2192 ListWorkEstimator        \u2502 (object count based)\n\u2502  - \"watch\" \u2192 ListWorkEstimator       \u2502 (with initial events)\n\u2502  - \"create\"/\"update\"/etc \u2192 Mutating  \u2502 (watch count based)\n\u2502  - default \u2192 MinimumSeats (1)        \u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2524\n\u2502 Returns WorkEstimate:                \u2502\n\u2502  - InitialSeats                      \u2502\n\u2502  - FinalSeats                        \u2502\n\u2502  - AdditionalLatency                 \u2502\n\u2502 Applied against MaxSeats limits      \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n#### Phase 3: QueueSet Processing\n\n**Case A: No Queues (DesiredNumQueues \u2264 0)**\n```\nif !canAccommodateSeats(workEstimate.MaxSeats()):\n    \u2192 Reject\nelse:\n    \u2192 Dispatch immediately (direct execution)\n```\n\n**Case B: With Queues (DesiredNumQueues > 0)**\n```\n1. Shuffle Sharding:\n   hand = dealer.Deal(hashValue)           # Random \"hand\" of queues\n   queueIdx = select_min_work_queue(hand)  # Pick least-loaded from hand\n\n2. Enqueue:\n   request.arrivalR = currentR\n   request.arrivalTime = now()\n   queue.requestsWaiting.Enqueue(request)\n   \n3. Try Dispatch:\n   dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked():\n       while (totRequests < currentCL) and (queues have work):\n           queue = fair_queue_selection()  # Pick queue by virtual time\n           request = queue.requestsWaiting.Dequeue()\n           queue.requestsExecuting.Add(request)\n           request.decision.Set(decisionExecute)\n           \n4. Request.Finish():\n   decision = request.decision.Get()  # Wait for dispatch decision\n   if decision == decisionExecute:\n       execute()  # Run the request\n   else:\n       return false  # Rejection/timeout\n```\n\n#### Phase 4: Virtual Time Management\n\n```go\n// queueset.go: syncTimeLocked() called at lock acquisition\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502 Update virtual time based on work    \u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2524\n\u2502 realNow = clock.Now()                \u2502\n\u2502 timeSinceLast = realNow - lastRealTime\u2502\n\u2502 rate = getVirtualTimeRatioLocked()   \u2502\n\u2502 incrR = rate * timeSinceLast         \u2502\n\u2502 currentR += incrR                    \u2502\n\u2502                                      \u2502\n\u2502 If currentR > highR:                 \u2502\n\u2502   advanceEpoch() \u2192 subtract rDecrement\u2502\n\u2502   (prevents overflow)                \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n#### Phase 5: Dispatch Decision\n\n```\nrequest.wait() called from request.Finish():\n\u251c\u2500 Decision retrieved from promise.Get()\n\u2502  (blocks until dispatched or context cancelled)\n\u251c\u2500 If decisionExecute:\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 Execute the handler\n\u251c\u2500 If decisionCancel:\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 Remove from queue (if still there)\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 Record rejection/timeout metrics\n\u2514\u2500 Return idle status\n```\n\n### 5. KEY INTERFACES AND TYPES\n\n#### Primary Interfaces\n\n**QueueSetFactory Interface** (`fairqueuing/interface.go`)\n```go\ntype QueueSetFactory interface {\n    BeginConstruction(\n        qCfg BOOTSTRAP CONFIGURATIONS\n\n**Default Priority Levels** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/apis/flowcontrol/bootstrap/default.go`):\n\n1. **\"exempt\"** (Mandatory)\n   - Type: Exempt\n   - Matches: `system:masters` group\n   - Resource: All verbs, groups, resources\n   - Non-Resource: All verbs and URLs\n\n2. **\"catch-all\"** (Mandatory)\n   - Type: Limited\n   - Concurrency Shares: 5\n   - Matches: All authenticated and unauthenticated users\n   - Fallback for requests without specific flow schema\n\n3. **\"system\"** (Suggested)\n   - Concurrency Shares: 30\n   - Queues: 64, HandSize: 6\n   - QueueLengthLimit: 50\n   - Lendable: 33%\n\n4. **\"node-high\"** (Suggested)\n   - Concurrency Shares: 40\n   - Queues: 64, HandSize: 6\n   - Lendable: 25%\n   - For node health reporting (kubelet, kube-proxy)\n\n5. **\"leader-election\"** (Suggested)\n   - Concurrency Shares: 10\n   - Queues: 16, HandSize: 4\n   - For controller leader election\n\n6. **\"workload-high\"** (Suggested)\n   - Concurrency Shares: 40\n   - Queues: 128, HandSize: 6\n   - Lendable: 50%\n   - For system workloads (scheduler, deployments)\n\n7. **\"workload-low\"** (Suggested)\n   - Concurrency Shares: 100\n   - Queues: 128, HandSize: 6\n   - Lendable: 90%\n\n8. **\"global-default\"** (Suggested)\n   - Concurrency Shares: 20\n   - Queues: 128, HandSize: 6\n   - Catch-all for remaining traffic\n\n### 7. METRICS AND OBSERVABILITY\n\n**Key Metrics Tracked:**\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_current_inqueue_requests_*` (per priority level)\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_current_executing_requests_*`\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_request_queue_length_*`\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_request_dispatch_no_accommodation_duration_seconds`\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_request_wait_duration_seconds`\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_seat_*` (seat utilization)\n- `apiserver_flowcontrol_demand_*` (demand forecasting)\n\n**Integrator-Based Tracking:**\n- Seat demand per priority level\n- Work distribution analysis\n- Smoothed utilization for borrowing decisions\n\n### 8. CONCURRENCY BORROWING ALGORITHM\n\n**Periodic Adjustment (every 10 seconds):**\n```\nFor each priority level:\n  1. Measure average seat demand (from integrator)\n  2. Calculate envelope = avg + stdDev\n  3. Smooth: smoothed = 0.977*smoothed + 0.023*envelope\n  4. Determine needed allocation\n  5. Adjust currentCL within [minCL, maxCL] bounds\n  \nConstraints:\n  - Total cannot exceed serverConcurrencyLimit\n  - Each level respects its min/max bounds\n  - Smoothing coefficient gives 5-minute half-life\n```\n\nThis comprehensive analysis covers the complete APF QueueSet subsystem architecture, implementation details, and request processing flow.",

"/*\nCopyright 2019 The Kubernetes Authors.\n\nLicensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\nyou may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\nYou may obtain a copy of the License at\n\n    http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n\nUnless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\ndistributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\nWITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\nSee the License for the specific language governing permissions and\nlimitations under the License.\n*/\n\npackage fairqueuing\n\nimport (\n\t\"context\"\n\n\t\"k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/debug\"\n\t\"k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/metrics\"\n\t\"k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request\"\n)\n\n// QueueSetFactory is used to create QueueSet objects.  Creation, like\n// config update, is done in two phases: the first phase consumes the\n// QueuingConfig and the second consumes the DispatchingConfig.  They\n// are separated so that errors from the first phase can be found\n// before committing to a concurrency allotment for the second.\ntype QueueSetFactory interface {\n\t// BeginConstruction does the first phase of creating a QueueSet.\n\t// The RatioedGaugePair observes number of requests,\n\t// execution covering just the regular phase.\n\t// The denominator for the waiting phase is\n\t// max(1, QueuingConfig.QueueLengthLimit) X max(1, QueuingConfig.DesiredNumQueues).\n\t// The RatioedGauge observes number of seats occupied through all phases of execution.\n\t// The denominator for all the ratioed concurrency gauges is supplied later in the DispatchingConfig.\n\t// The Gauge observes the seat demand (executing + queued seats).\n\tBeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, metrics.RatioedGaugePair, metrics.RatioedGauge, metrics.Gauge) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\n}\n\n// QueueSetCompleter finishes the two-step process of creating or\n// reconfiguring a QueueSet\ntype QueueSetCompleter interface {\n\t// Complete returns a QueueSet configured by the given\n\t// dispatching configuration.\n\tComplete(DispatchingConfig) QueueSet\n}\n\n// QueueSet is the abstraction for the queuing and dispatching\n// functionality of one non-exempt priority level.  It covers the\n// functionality described in the \"Assignment to a Queue\", \"Queuing\",\n// and \"Dispatching\" sections of\n// https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/blob/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/1040-priority-and-fairness/README.md\n// .  Some day we may have connections between priority levels, but\n// today is not that day.\ntype QueueSet interface {\n\t// BeginConfigChange starts the two-step process of updating the\n\t// configuration.  No change is made until Complete is called.  If\n\t// `C := X.BeginConstruction(q)` then `C.Complete(d)` returns the\n\t// same value `X`.  If the QueuingConfig's DesiredNumQueues field\n\t// is zero then the other queuing-specific config parameters are\n\t// not changed, so that the queues continue draining as before.\n\t// In any case, reconfiguration does not discard any queue unless\n\t// and until it is undesired and empty.\n\tBeginConfigChange(QueuingConfig) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\n\n\t// IsIdle returns a bool indicating whether the QueueSet was idle\n\t// at the moment of the return.  Idle means the QueueSet has zero\n\t// requests queued and zero executing.  This bit can change only\n\t// (1) during a call to StartRequest and (2) during a call to\n\t// Request::Finish.  In the latter case idleness can only change\n\t// from false to true.\n\tIsIdle() bool\n\n\t// StartRequest begins the process of handling a request.  If the\n\t// request gets queued and the number of queues is greater than 1\n\t// then StartRequest uses the given hashValue as the source of\n\t// entropy as it shuffle-shards the request into a queue.  The\n\t// descr1 and descr2 values play no role in the logic but appear\n\t// in log messages.  This method always returns quickly (without\n\t// waiting for the request to be dequeued).  If this method\n\t// returns a nil Request value then caller should reject the\n\t// request and the returned bool indicates whether the QueueSet\n\t// was idle at the moment of the return.  Otherwise idle==false\n\t// and the client must call the Finish method of the Request\n\t// exactly once.\n\tStartRequest(ctx context.Context, width *request.WorkEstimate, hashValue uint64, flowDistinguisher, fsName string, descr1, descr2 interface{}, queueNoteFn QueueNoteFn) (req Request, idle bool)\n\n\t// Dump saves and returns the instant internal state of the queue-set.\n\t// Note that dumping process will stop the queue-set from proceeding\n\t// any requests.\n\t// For debugging only.\n\tDump(includeRequestDetails bool) debug.QueueSetDump\n}\n\n// QueueNoteFn is called when a request enters and leaves a queue\ntype QueueNoteFn func(inQueue bool)\n\n// Request represents the remainder of the handling of one request\ntype Request interface {\n\t// Finish determines whether to execute or reject the request and\n\t// invokes `execute` if the decision is to execute the request.\n\t// The returned `idle bool` value indicates whether the QueueSet\n\t// was idle when the value was calculated, but might no longer be\n\t// accurate by the time the client examines that value.\n\tFinish(execute func()) (idle bool)\n}\n\n// QueuingConfig defines the configuration of the queuing aspect of a QueueSet.\ntype QueuingConfig struct {\n\t// Name is used to identify a queue set, allowing for descriptive information about its intended use\n\tName string\n\n\t// DesiredNumQueues is the number of queues that the API says\n\t// should exist now.  This may be non-positive, in which case\n\t// QueueLengthLimit, and HandSize are ignored.\n\t// A value of zero means to respect the ConcurrencyLimit of the DispatchingConfig.\n\t// A negative value means to always dispatch immediately upon arrival\n\t// (i.e., the requests are \"exempt\" from limitation).\n\tDesiredNumQueues int\n\n\t// QueueLengthLimit is the maximum number of requests that may be waiting in a given queue at a time\n\tQueueLengthLimit int\n\n\t// HandSize is a parameter of shuffle sharding.  Upon arrival of a request, a queue is chosen by randomly\n\t// dealing a \"hand\" of this many queues and then picking one of minimum length.\n\tHandSize int\n}\n\n// DispatchingConfig defines the configuration of the dispatching aspect of a QueueSet.\ntype DispatchingConfig struct {\n\t// ConcurrencyLimit is the maximum number of requests of this QueueSet that may be executing at a time\n\tConcurrencyLimit int\n\n\t// ConcurrencyDenominator is used in relative metrics of concurrency.\n\t// It equals ConcurrencyLimit except when that is zero.\n\tConcurrencyDenominator int\n}"

"/*\nCopyright 2021 The Kubernetes Authors.\n\nLicensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\nyou may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\nYou may obtain a IS\" BASIS,\nWITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\nSee the License for the specific language governing permissions and\nlimitations under the License.\n*/\n\npackage queueset\n\nimport (\n\t\"container/list\"\n)\n\n// removeFromFIFOFunc removes a designated element from the list\n// if that element is in the list.\n// The complexity of the runtime cost is O(1).\n// The returned value is the element removed, if indeed one was removed,\n// otherwise `nil`.\ntype removeFromFIFOFunc func() *request\n\n// walkFunc is called for each request in the list in the\n// oldest -> newest order.\n// ok: if walkFunc returns false then the iteration stops immediately.\n// walkFunc may remove the given request from the fifo,\n// but may not mutate the fifo in any othe way.\ntype walkFunc func(*request) (ok bool)\n\n// Internal interface to abstract out the implementation details\n// of the underlying list used to maintain the requests.\n//\n// Note that a fifo, including the removeFromFIFOFuncs returned from Enqueue,\n// is not safe for concurrent use by multiple goroutines.\ntype fifo interface {\n\t// Enqueue enqueues the specified request into the list and\n\t// returns a removeFromFIFOFunc function that can be used to remove the\n\t// request from the list\n\tEnqueue(*request) removeFromFIFOFunc\n\n\t// Dequeue pulls out the oldest request from the list.\n\tDequeue() (*request, bool)\n\n\t// Peek returns the oldest request without removing it.\n\tPeek() (*request, bool)\n\n\t// Length returns the number of requests in the list.\n\tLength() int\n\n\t// QueueSum returns the sum of initial seats, final seats, and\n\t// additional latency aggregated from all requests in this queue.\n\tQueueSum() queueSum\n\n\t// Walk iterates through the list in order of oldest -> newest\n\t// and executes the specified walkFunc for each request in that order.\n\t//\n\t// if the specified walkFunc returns false the Walk function\n\t// stops the walk an returns immediately.\n\tWalk(walkFunc)\n}\n\n// the FIFO list implementation is not safe for concurrent use by multiple\n// goroutines.\ntype requestFIFO struct {\n\t*list.List\n\n\tsum queueSum\n}\n\nfunc newRequestFIFO() fifo {\n\treturn &requestFIFO{\n\t\tList: list.New(),\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (l *requestFIFO) Length() int {\n\treturn l.Len()\n}\n\nfunc (l *requestFIFO) QueueSum() queueSum {\n\treturn l.sum\n}\n\nfunc (l *requestFIFO) Enqueue(req *request) removeFromFIFOFunc {\n\te := l.PushBack(req)\n\taddToQueueSum(&l.sum, req)\n\n\treturn func() *request {\n\t\tif e.Value == nil {\n\t\t\treturn nil\n\t\t}\n\t\tl.Remove(e)\n\t\te.Value = nil\n\t\tdeductFromQueueSum(&l.sum, req)\n\t\treturn req\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (l *requestFIFO) Dequeue() (*request, bool) {\n\treturn l.getFirst(true)\n}\n\nfunc (l *requestFIFO) Peek() (*request, bool) {\n\treturn l.getFirst(false)\n}\n\nfunc (l *requestFIFO) getFirst(remove bool) (*request, bool) {\n\te := l.Front()\n\tif e == nil {\n\t\treturn nil, false\n\t}\n\n\tif remove {\n\t\tdefer func() {\n\t\t\tl.Remove(e)\n\t\t\te.Value = nil\n\t\t}()\n\t}\n\n\trequest, ok := e.Value.(*request)\n\tif remove && ok {\n\t\tdeductFromQueueSum(&l.sum, request)\n\t}\n\treturn request, ok\n}\n\nfunc (l *requestFIFO) Walk(f walkFunc) {\n\tvar next *list.Element\n\tfor current := l.Front(); current != nil; current = next {\n\t\tnext = current.Next() // f is allowed to remove current\n\t\tif r, ok := current.Value.(*request); ok {\n\t\t\tif !f(r) {\n\t\t\t\treturn\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc addToQueueSum(sum *queueSum, req *request) {\n\tsum.InitialSeatsSum += req.InitialSeats()\n\tsum.MaxSeatsSum += req.MaxSeats()\n\tsum.TotalWorkSum += req.totalWork()\n}\n\nfunc deductFromQueueSum(sum *queueSum, req *request) {\n\tsum.InitialSeatsSum -= req.InitialSeats()\n\tsum.MaxSeatsSum -= req.MaxSeats()\n\tsum.TotalWorkSum -= req.totalWork()\n}"

flowSchemaName, priorityLevelName)\n\tcase \"watch\":\n\t\t// WATCH supports `SendInitialEvents` option, which effectively means\n\t\t// that is starts with sending of the contents of a corresponding \"update\", \"patch\", \"delete\":\n\t\treturn e.mutatingWorkEstimator.EstimateWork(r, flowSchemaName, priorityLevelName)\n\t}\n\n\treturn WorkEstimate{InitialSeats: e.minimumSeats}\n}"

"/*\nCopyright 2019 The Kubernetes Authors.\n\nLicensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\nyou may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\nYou may obtain a copy of the License at\n\n    http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n\nUnless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\ndistributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\nWITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\nSee the License for the specific language governing permissions and\nlimitations under the License.\n*/\n\npackage promise\n\nimport (\n\t\"context\"\n\t\"sync\"\n)\n\n// promise implements the WriteOnce interface.\ntype promise struct {\n\tdoneCtx context.Context\n\tdoneVal interface{}\n\tsetCh   chan struct{}\n\tonceler sync.Once\n\tvalue   interface{}\n}\n\nvar _ WriteOnce = &promise{}\n\n// NewWriteOnce makes a new thread-safe WriteOnce.\n//\n// If `initial` is non-nil then that value is Set at creation time.\n//\n// If a `Get` is waiting soon after the channel associated with the\n// `doneCtx` becomes selectable (which never happens for the nil\n// channel) then `Set(doneVal)` effectively happens at that time.\nfunc NewWriteOnce(initial interface{}, doneCtx context.Context, doneVal interface{}) WriteOnce {\n\tp := &promise{\n\t\tdoneCtx: doneCtx,\n\t\tdoneVal: doneVal,\n\t\tsetCh:   make(chan struct{}),\n\t}\n\tif initial != nil {\n\t\tp.Set(initial)\n\t}\n\treturn p\n}\n\nfunc (p *promise) Get() interface{} {\n\tselect {\n\tcase <-p.setCh:\n\tcase <-p.doneCtx.Done():\n\t\tp.Set(p.doneVal)\n\t}\n\treturn p.value\n}\n\nfunc (p *promise) Set(value interface{}) bool {\n\tvar ans bool\n\tp.onceler.Do(func() {\n\t\tp.value = value\n\t\tclose(p.setCh)\n\t\tans = true\n\t})\n\treturn ans\n}"

"/*\nCopyright 2019 The Kubernetes Authors.\n\nLicensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\nyou may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\nYou may obtain a copy of the License at\n\n    http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n\nUnless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\ndistributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\nWITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\nSee the License for the specific language governing permissions and\nlimitations under the License.\n*/\n\npackage fairqueuing\n\nimport (\n\t\"math\"\n\t\"sync\"\n\t\"time\"\n\n\tfcmetrics \"k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/metrics\"\n\n\t\"k8s.io/utils/clock\"\n)\n\n// Integrator computes the moments of some variable X over time as\n// read from a particular clock. math.IsNaN(x.Deviation) && math.IsNaN(y.Deviation))\n}\n\ntype integrator struct {\n\tname  string\n\tclock clock.PassiveClock\n\tsync.Mutex\n\tlastTime time.Time\n\tx        float64\n\tmoments  Moments\n\tmin, max float64\n}\n\n// NewNamedIntegrator makes one that uses the given clock and name\nfunc NewNamedIntegrator(clock clock.PassiveClock, name string) Integrator {\n\treturn &integrator{\n\t\tname:     name,\n\t\tclock:    clock,\n\t\tlastTime: clock.Now(),\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (igr *integrator) Set(x float64) {\n\tigr.Lock()\n\tigr.setLocked(x)\n\tigr.Unlock()\n}\n\nfunc (igr *integrator) Add(deltaX float64) {\n\tigr.Lock()\n\tigr.setLocked(igr.x + deltaX)\n\tigr.Unlock()\n}\n\nfunc (igr *integrator) Inc() {\n\tigr.Add(1)\n}\n\nfunc (igr *integrator) Dec() {\n\tigr.Add(-1)\n}\n\nfunc (igr *integrator) SetToCurrentTime() {\n\tigr.Set(float64(time.Now().UnixNano()))\n}\n\nfunc (igr *integrator) setLocked(x float64) {\n\tigr.updateLocked()\n\tigr.x = x\n\tif x < igr.min {\n\t\tigr.min = x\n\t}\n\tif x > igr.max {\n\t\tigr.max = x\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (igr *integrator) updateLocked() {\n\tnow := igr.clock.Now()\n\tdt := now.Sub(igr.lastTime).Seconds()\n\tigr.lastTime = now\n\tigr.moments = igr.moments.Add(ConstantMoments(dt, igr.x))\n}\n\nfunc (igr *integrator) GetResults() IntegratorResults {\n\tigr.Lock()\n\tdefer igr.Unlock()\n\treturn igr.getResultsLocked()\n}\n\nfunc (igr *integrator) Reset() IntegratorResults {\n\tigr.Lock()\n\tdefer igr.Unlock()\n\tresults := igr.getResultsLocked()\n\tigr.moments = Moments{}\n\tigr.min = igr.x\n\tigr.max = igr.x\n\treturn results\n}\n\nfunc (igr *integrator) getResultsLocked() (results IntegratorResults) {\n\tigr.updateLocked()\n\tresults.Min, results.Max = igr.min, igr.max\n\tresults.Duration = igr.moments.ElapsedSeconds\n\tresults.Average, results.Deviation = igr.moments.AvgAndStdDev()\n\treturn\n}\n\n// Moments are the integrals of the 0, 1, and 2 powers of some\n// variable X over some range of time.\ntype Moments struct {\n\tElapsedSeconds float64 // integral of dt\n\tIntegralX      float64 // integral of x dt\n\tIntegralXX     float64 // integral of x*x dt\n}\n\n// ConstantMoments is for a constant X\nfunc ConstantMoments(dt, x float64) Moments {\n\treturn Moments{\n\t\tElapsedSeconds: dt,\n\t\tIntegralX:      x * dt,\n\t\tIntegralXX:     x * x * dt,\n\t}\n}\n\n// Add combines over two ranges of time\nfunc (igr Moments) Add(ogr Moments) Moments {\n\treturn Moments{\n\t\tElapsedSeconds: igr.ElapsedSeconds + ogr.ElapsedSeconds,\n\t\tIntegralX:      igr.IntegralX + ogr.IntegralX,\n\t\tIntegralXX:     igr.IntegralXX + ogr.IntegralXX,\n\t}\n}\n\n// Sub finds the difference between a range of time and a subrange\nfunc (igr Moments) Sub(ogr Moments) Moments {\n\treturn Moments{\n\t\tElapsedSeconds: igr.ElapsedSeconds - ogr.ElapsedSeconds,\n\t\tIntegralX:      igr.IntegralX - ogr.IntegralX,\n\t\tIntegralXX:     igr.IntegralXX - ogr.IntegralXX,\n\t}\n}\n\n// AvgAndStdDev returns the average and standard devation\nfunc (igr Moments) AvgAndStdDev() (float64, float64) {\n\tif igr.ElapsedSeconds <= 0 {\n\t\treturn math.NaN(), math.NaN()\n\t}\n\tavg := igr.IntegralX / igr.ElapsedSeconds\n\t// standard deviation is sqrt( average( (x - xbar)^2 ) )\n\t// = sqrt( Integral( x^2 + xbar^2 -2*x*xbar dt ) / Duration )\n\t// = sqrt( ( Integral( x^2 dt ) + Duration * xbar^2 - 2*xbar*Integral(x dt) ) / Duration)\n\t// = sqrt( Integral(x^2 dt)/Duration - xbar^2 )\n\tvariance := igr.IntegralXX/igr.ElapsedSeconds - avg*avg\n\tif variance >= 0 {\n\t\treturn avg, math.Sqrt(variance)\n\t}\n\treturn avg, math.NaN()\n}"

"/*\nCopyright 2019 The Kubernetes Authors.\n\nLicensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\nyou may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\nYou may obtain a copy of the License at\n\n    http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n\nUnless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\ndistributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\nWITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\nSee the License for the specific language governing permissions and\nlimitations under the License.\n*/\n\npackage shufflesharding\n\nimport (\n\t\"fmt\"\n\t\"math\"\n)\n\n// MaxHashBits is the max bit length which can be used from hash value.\n// If we use all bits of hash value, the critical(last) card shuffled by\n// Dealer will be uneven to 2:3 (first half:second half) at most,\n// in order to reduce this unevenness to 32:33, we set MaxHashBits to 60 here.\nconst MaxHashBits = 60\n\n// RequiredEntropyBits makes a quick and slightly conservative estimate of the number\n// of bits of hash value that are consumed in shuffle sharding a deck of the given size\n// to a hand of the given size.  The result is meaningful only if\n// 1 <= handSize <= deckSize <= 1<<26.\nfunc RequiredEntropyBits(deckSize, handSize int) int {\n\treturn int(math.Ceil(math.Log2(float64(deckSize)) * float64(handSize)))\n}\n\n// Dealer contains some necessary parameters and provides some methods for shuffle sharding.\n// Dealer is thread-safe.\ntype Dealer struct {\n\tdeckSize int\n\thandSize int\n}\n\n// NewDealer will create a Dealer with the given deckSize and handSize, will return error when\n// deckSize or handSize is invalid as below.\n// 1. deckSize or handSize is not positive\n// 2. handSize is greater than deckSize\n// 3. deckSize is impractically large (greater than 1<<26)\n// 4. required entropy bits of deckSize and handSize is greater than MaxHashBits\nfunc NewDealer(deckSize, handSize int) (*Dealer, error) {\n\tif deckSize <= 0 || handSize <= 0 {\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"deckSize %d or handSize %d is not positive\", deckSize, handSize)\n\t}\n\tif handSize > deckSize {\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"handSize %d is greater than deckSize %d\", handSize, deckSize)\n\t}\n\tif deckSize > 1<<26 {\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"deckSize %d is impractically large\", deckSize)\n\t}\n\tif RequiredEntropyBits(deckSize, handSize) > MaxHashBits {\n\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"required entropy bits of deckSize %d and handSize %d is greater than %d\", deckSize, handSize, MaxHashBits)\n\t}\n\n\treturn &Dealer{\n\t\tdeckSize: deckSize,\n\t\thandSize: handSize,\n\t}, nil\n}\n\n// Deal shuffles a card deck and deals a hand of cards, using the given hashValue as the source of entropy.\n// The deck size and hand size are properties of the Dealer.\n// This function synchronously makes sequential calls to pick, one for each dealt card.\n// Each card is identified by an integer in the range [0, deckSize).\n// For example, for deckSize=128 and handSize=4 this function might call pick(14); pick(73); pick(119); pick(26).\nfunc (d *Dealer) Deal(hashValue uint64, pick func(int)) {\n\t// 15 is the largest possible value of handSize\n\tvar remainders [15]int\n\n\tfor i := 0; i < d.handSize; i++ {\n\t\thashValueNext := hashValue / uint64(d.deckSize-i)\n\t\tremainders[i] = int(hashValue - uint64(d.deckSize-i)*hashValueNext)\n\t\thashValue = hashValueNext\n\t}\n\n\tfor i := 0; i < d.handSize; i++ {\n\t\tcard := remainders[i]\n\t\tfor j := i; j > 0; j-- {\n\t\t\tif card >= remainders[j-1] {\n\t\t\t\tcard++\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\tpick(card)\n\t}\n}\n\n// DealIntoHand shuffles and deals according to the Dealer's parameters,\n// using the given hashValue as the source of entropy and then\n// returns the dealt cards as a slice of `int`.\n// If `hand` has the correct length as Dealer's handSize, it will be used as-is and no allocations will be made.\n// If `hand` is nil or too small, it will be extended (performing an allocation).\n// If `hand` is too large, a sub-slice will be returned.\nfunc (d *Dealer) DealIntoHand(hashValue uint64, hand []int) []int {\n\th := hand[:0]\n\td.Deal(hashValue, func(card int) { h = append(h, card) })\n\treturn h\n}"

{\n\tqs.lockAndSyncTime(ctx)\n\tdefer qs.lock.Unlock()\n\n\tif qCfg.DesiredNumQueues > 0 {\n\t\t// Adding queues is the only thing that requires immediate action\n\t\t// Removing queues is handled by append(qs.queues,\n\t\t\t\tcreateQueues(qCfg.DesiredNumQueues-numQueues, len(qs.queues))...)\n\t\t}\n\t} else {\n\t\tqCfg.QueueLengthLimit = qs.qCfg.QueueLengthLimit\n\t\tqCfg.HandSize = qs.qCfg.HandSize\n\t}\n\n\tqs.qCfg = qCfg\n\tqs.dCfg = dCfg\n\tqs.dealer = dealer\n\tqll := qCfg.QueueLengthLimit\n\tif qll < 1 {\n\t\tqll = 1\n\t}\n\tif qCfg.DesiredNumQueues > 0 {\n\t\tqll *= qCfg.DesiredNumQueues\n\t}\n\tqs.reqsGaugePair.RequestsWaiting.SetDenominator(float64(qll))\n\tqs.reqsGaugePair.RequestsExecuting.SetDenominator(float64(dCfg.ConcurrencyDenominator))\n\tqs.execSeatsGauge.SetDenominator(float64(dCfg.ConcurrencyDenominator))\n\n\tqs.dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()\n}\n\n// A decision about a request\ntype requestDecision int\n\n// Values passed through a request's decision\nconst (\n\t// Serve this one\n\tdecisionExecute requestDecision = iota\n\n\t// This one's context timed out / was canceled\n\tdecisionCancel\n)\n\n// StartRequest begins the process of handling a request.  We take the\n// approach of updating the metrics about total requests queued and\n// executing at each point where there is a change in that quantity,\n// because the metrics --- and only the metrics --- track that\n// quantity per FlowSchema.\n// The queueSet's promiseFactory is invoked once if the returned Request is non-nil,\n// not invoked if the Request is nil.\nfunc (qs *queueSet) StartRequest(ctx context.Context, workEstimate *fqrequest.WorkEstimate, hashValue uint64, flowDistinguisher, fsName string, descr1, descr2 interface{}, queueNoteFn fq.QueueNoteFn) (fq.Request, bool) {\n\tqs.lockAndSyncTime(ctx)\n\tdefer qs.lock.Unlock()\n\tvar req *request\n\n\t// ========================================================================\n\t// Step 0:\n\t// Apply only concurrency limit, if zero queues desired\n\tif qs.qCfg.DesiredNumQueues < 1 {\n\t\tif !qs.canAccommodateSeatsLocked(workEstimate.MaxSeats()) {\n\t\t\tklog.V(5).Infof(\"QS(%s): rejecting request %q %#+v %#+v because %d seats are asked for, %d seats are in use (%d are executing) and the limit is %d\",\n\t\t\t\tqs.qCfg.Name, fsName, descr1, descr2, workEstimate, qs.totSeatsInUse, qs.totRequestsExecuting, qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit)\n\t\t\tqs.totRequestsRejected++\n\t\t\tmetrics.AddReject(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, fsName, \"concurrency-limit\")\n\t\t\treturn nil, qs.isIdleLocked()\n\t\t}\n\t\treq = qs.dispatchSansQueueLocked(ctx, workEstimate, flowDistinguisher, fsName, descr1, descr2)\n\t\treturn req, false\n\t}\n\n\t// ========================================================================\n\t// Step 1:\n\t// 1) Start with shuffle sharding, to pick a queue.\n\t// 2) Reject current request if there is not enough concurrency shares and\n\t// we are at max queue length\n\t// 3) If not rejected, create a request and enqueue\n\treq = qs.shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked(ctx, workEstimate, hashValue, flowDistinguisher, fsName, descr1, descr2, queueNoteFn)\n\t// req == nil means that the request was rejected - no remaining\n\t// concurrency shares and at max queue length already\n\tif req == nil {\n\t\tklog.V(5).Infof(\"QS(%s): rejecting request %q %#+v %#+v due to queue full\", qs.qCfg.Name, fsName, descr1, descr2)\n\t\tqs.totRequestsRejected++\n\t\tmetrics.AddReject(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, fsName, \"queue-full\")\n\t\treturn nil, qs.isIdleLocked()\n\t}\n\n\t// ========================================================================\n\t// Step 2:\n\t// The next step is to invoke the method that dequeues as much\n\t// as possible.\n\t// This method runs a loop, as long as there are non-empty\n\t// queues and the number currently executing is less than the\n\t// assured concurrency value.  The body of the loop uses the\n\t// fair queuing technique to pick a queue and dispatch a\n\t// request from that queue.\n\tqs.dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()\n\n\treturn req, false\n}\n\n// ordinaryPromiseFactoryFactory is the promiseFactoryFactory that\n// a queueSetFactory would ordinarily use.\n// Test code might use something different.\nfunc ordinaryPromiseFactoryFactory(qs *queueSet) promiseFactory {\n\treturn promise.NewWriteOnce\n}\n\n// MaxSeats returns the maximum number of seats this request requires, it is\n// the maxumum of the two - WorkEstimate.InitialSeats, WorkEstimate.FinalSeats.\nfunc (req *request) MaxSeats() int {\n\treturn req.workEstimate.MaxSeats()\n}\n\nfunc (req *request) InitialSeats() int {\n\treturn int(req.workEstimate.InitialSeats)\n}\n\nfunc (req *request) NoteQueued(inQueue bool) {\n\tif req.queueNoteFn != nil {\n\t\treq.queueNoteFn(inQueue)\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (req *request) Finish(execFn func()) bool {\n\texec, idle := req.wait()\n\tif !exec {\n\t\treturn idle\n\t}\n\tfunc() {\n\t\tdefer func() {\n\t\t\tidle = req.qs.finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible(req)\n\t\t}()\n\n\t\texecFn()\n\t}()\n\n\treturn idle\n}\n\nfunc (req *request) wait() (bool, bool) {\n\tqs := req.qs\n\n\t// ========================================================================\n\t// Step 3:\n\t// The final step is to wait on a decision from\n\t// somewhere and then act on it.\n\tdecisionAny := req.decision.Get()\n\tqs.lockAndSyncTime(req.ctx)\n\tdefer qs.lock.Unlock()\n\tif req.waitStarted {\n\t\t// This can not happen, because the client is forbidden to\n\t\t// call Wait twice on the same request\n\t\tklog.Errorf(\"Duplicate call to the Wait method!  Immediately returning execute=false.  QueueSet=%s, startTime=%s, descr1=%#+v, descr2=%#+v\", req.qs.qCfg.Name, req.startTime, req.descr1, req.descr2)\n\t\treturn false, qs.isIdleLocked()\n\t}\n\treq.waitStarted = true\n\tswitch decisionAny {\n\tcase decisionCancel: // handle in code following this switch\n\tcase decisionExecute:\n\t\tklog.V(5).Infof(\"QS(%s): Dispatching request %#+v %#+v from its queue\", qs.qCfg.Name, req.descr1, req.descr2)\n\t\treturn true, false\n\tdefault:\n\t\t// This can not happen, all possible values are handled above\n\t\tklog.Errorf(\"QS(%s): Impossible decision (type %T, value %#+v) for request %#+v %#+v!  Treating as cancel\", qs.qCfg.Name, decisionAny, decisionAny, req.descr1, req.descr2)\n\t}\n\t// TODO(aaron-prindle) add metrics for this case\n\tklog.V(5).Infof(\"QS(%s): Ejecting request %#+v %#+v from its queue\", qs.qCfg.Name, req.descr1, req.descr2)\n\t// remove the request from the queue as its queue wait time has exceeded\n\tqueue := req.queue\n\tif req.removeFromQueueLocked() != nil {\n\t\tdefer qs.boundNextDispatchLocked(queue)\n\t\tqs.totRequestsWaiting--\n\t\tqs.totSeatsWaiting -= req.MaxSeats()\n\t\tqs.totRequestsRejected++\n\t\tqs.totRequestsCancelled++\n\t\tmetrics.AddReject(req.ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, req.fsName, \"time-out\")\n\t\tmetrics.AddRequestsInQueues(req.ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, req.fsName, -1)\n\t\tmetrics.AddSeatsInQueues(req.ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, req.fsName, -req.MaxSeats())\n\t\treq.NoteQueued(false)\n\t\tqs.reqsGaugePair.RequestsWaiting.Add(-1)\n\t\tqs.seatDemandIntegrator.Set(float64(qs.totSeatsInUse + qs.totSeatsWaiting))\n\t}\n\treturn false, qs.isIdleLocked()\n}\n\nfunc (qs *queueSet) IsIdle() bool {\n\tqs.lock.Lock()\n\tdefer qs.lock.Unlock()\n\treturn qs.isIdleLocked()\n}\n\nfunc (qs *queueSet) isIdleLocked() bool {\n\treturn qs.totRequestsWaiting == 0 && qs.totRequestsExecuting == 0\n}\n\n// lockAndSyncTime acquires the lock and updates the virtual time.\n// Doing them together avoids the mistake of modifying some queue state\n// before calling syncTimeLocked.\nfunc (qs *queueSet) lockAndSyncTime(ctx context.Context) {\n\tqs.lock.Lock()\n\tqs.syncTimeLocked(ctx)\n}\n\n// syncTimeLocked updates the virtual time based on the assumption\n// that the current state of the queues has been in effect since\n// `qs.lastRealTime`.  Thus, it should be invoked after acquiring the\n// lock and before modifying the state of any queue.\nfunc (qs *queueSet) syncTimeLocked(ctx context.Context) {\n\trealNow := qs.clock.Now()\n\ttimeSinceLast := realNow.Sub(qs.lastRealTime)\n\tqs.lastRealTime = realNow\n\tprevR := qs.currentR\n\tincrR := fqrequest.SeatsTimesDuration(qs.getVirtualTimeRatioLocked(), timeSinceLast)\n\tqs.currentR = prevR + incrR\n\tswitch {\n\tcase prevR > qs.currentR:\n\t\tklog.ErrorS(errors.New(\"queueset::currentR overflow\"), \"Overflow\", \"QS\", qs.qCfg.Name, \"when\", realNow.Format(nsTimeFmt), \"prevR\", prevR, \"incrR\", incrR, \"currentR\", qs.currentR)\n\tcase qs.currentR >= highR:\n\t\tqs.advanceEpoch(ctx, realNow, incrR)\n\t}\n\tmetrics.SetCurrentR(qs.qCfg.Name, qs.currentR.ToFloat())\n}\n\n// rDecrement is the amount by which the progress meter R is wound backwards\n// when needed to avoid overflow.\nconst rDecrement = fqrequest.MaxSeatSeconds / 2\n\n// highR is the threshold that triggers advance of the epoch.\n// That is, decrementing the global progress meter R by rDecrement.\nconst highR = rDecrement + rDecrement/2\n\n// advanceEpoch subtracts rDecrement from the global progress meter R\n// and all the readings that have been taked from that meter.\n// The now and incrR parameters are only used to add info to the log messages.\nfunc (qs *queueSet) advanceEpoch(ctx context.Context, now time.Time, incrR fqrequest.SeatSeconds) {\n\toldR := qs.currentR\n\tqs.currentR -= rDecrement\n\tklog.InfoS(\"Advancing epoch\", \"QS\", qs.qCfg.Name, \"when\", now.Format(nsTimeFmt), \"oldR\", oldR, \"newR\", qs.currentR, \"incrR\", incrR)\n\tsuccess := true\n\tfor qIdx, queue := range qs.queues {\n\t\tif queue.requestsWaiting.Length() == 0 && queue.requestsExecuting.Len() == 0 {\n\t\t\t// Do not just decrement, the value could be quite outdated.\n\t\t\t// It is safe to reset to zero in this case, because the next request\n\t\t\t// will overwrite the zero with `qs.currentR`.\n\t\t\tqueue.nextDispatchR = 0\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\t\toldNextDispatchR := queue.nextDispatchR\n\t\tqueue.nextDispatchR -= rDecrement\n\t\tif queue.nextDispatchR > oldNextDispatchR {\n\t\t\tklog.ErrorS(errors.New(\"queue::nextDispatchR underflow\"), \"Underflow\", \"QS\", qs.qCfg.Name, \"queue\", qIdx, \"oldNextDispatchR\", oldNextDispatchR, \"newNextDispatchR\", queue.nextDispatchR, \"incrR\", incrR)\n\t\t\tsuccess = false\n\t\t}\n\t\tqueue.requestsWaiting.Walk(func(req *request) bool {\n\t\t\toldArrivalR := req.arrivalR\n\t\t\treq.arrivalR -= rDecrement\n\t\t\tif req.arrivalR > oldArrivalR {\n\t\t\t\tklog.ErrorS(errors.New(\"request::arrivalR underflow\"), \"Underflow\", \"QS\", qs.qCfg.Name, \"queue\", qIdx, \"request\", *req, \"oldArrivalR\", oldArrivalR, \"incrR\", incrR)\n\t\t\t\tsuccess = false\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t})\n\t}\n\tmetrics.AddEpochAdvance(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, success)\n}\n\n// getVirtualTimeRatio calculates the rate at which virtual time has\n// been advancing, according to the logic in `doc.go`.\nfunc (qs *queueSet) getVirtualTimeRatioLocked() float64 {\n\tactiveQueues := 0\n\tseatsRequested := 0\n\tfor _, queue := range qs.queues == 0 {\n\t\treturn 0\n\t}\n\treturn math.Min(float64(seatsRequested), float64(qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit)) / float64(activeQueues)\n}\n\n// shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked encapsulates the logic required\n// to validate and enqueue a request for the queueSet/QueueSet:\n// 1) Start with shuffle sharding, to pick a queue.\n// 2) Reject current request if there is not enough concurrency shares and\n// we are at max queue length\n// 3) If not rejected, create a request and enqueue\n// returns the enqueud request on a successful enqueue\n// returns nil in the case that there is no available concurrency or\n// the queuelengthlimit has been reached\nfunc (qs *queueSet) shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked(ctx context.Context, workEstimate *fqrequest.WorkEstimate, hashValue uint64,       qs.clock.Now(),\n\t\tarrivalR:          qs.currentR,\n\t\tqueue:             queue,\n\t\tdescr1:            descr1,\n\t\tdescr2:            descr2,\n\t\tqueueNoteFn: qs.qCfg.Name, fsName, queue.requestsWaiting.Length())\n\treturn req\n}\n\n// shuffleShardLocked uses shuffle sharding to select a queue index\n// using the given hashValue and the shuffle sharding parameters of the queueSet.\nfunc (qs *queueSet) shuffleShardLocked(hashValue uint64, descr1, descr2 interface{}) int {\n\tvar backHand [8]int\n\t// Deal into a data structure, so that the order of visit below is not necessarily the order of the deal.\n\t// This removes bias in the case of flows with overlapping hands.\n\thand := qs.dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, backHand[:])\n\thandSize := len(hand)\n\toffset := qs.enqueues % handSize\n\tqs.enqueues++\n\tbestQueueIdx := -1\n\tminQueueSeatSeconds := fqrequest.MaxSeatSeconds\n\tfor i := 0; i < handSize; i++ {\n\t\tqueueIdx := hand[(offset+i)%handSize]\n\t\tqueue := qs.queues[queueIdx]\n\t\tqueueSum := queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum()\n\n\t\t// this is the total amount of work in seat-seconds for requests\n\t\t// waiting in this queue, we will select the queue with the minimum."

Thus, it should be invoked after acquiring the\n// lock and before modifying the state of any queue.\nfunc (qs *queueSet) syncTimeLocked(ctx context.Context) {\n\trealNow := qs.clock.Now()\n\ttimeSinceLast := realNow.Sub(qs.lastRealTime)\n\tqs.lastRealTime = realNow\n\tprevR := qs.currentR\n\tincrR := fqrequest.SeatsTimesDuration(qs.getVirtualTimeRatioLocked(), timeSinceLast)\n\tqs.currentR = prevR + incrR\n\tswitch {\n\tcase prevR > qs.currentR:\n\t\tklog.ErrorS(errors.New(\"queueset::currentR overflow\"), \"Overflow\", \"QS\", qs.qCfg.Name, \n\t\t\t\"when\", realNow.Format(nsTimeFmt), \"prevR\", prevR, \"incrR\", incrR, \"currentR\", qs.currentR)\n\tcase qs.currentR >= highR:\n\t\tqs.advanceEpoch(ctx, realNow, incrR)\n\t}\n\tmetrics.SetCurrentR(qs.qCfg.Name, qs.currentR.ToFloat())\n}\n\n// Constants for epoch advancement (overflow prevention)\nconst rDecrement = fqrequest.MaxSeatSeconds / 2\nconst highR = rDecrement + rDecrement/2  // Triggers epoch advance at this threshold\n\n// advanceEpoch subtracts rDecrement from the global progress meter R\n// and all the readings that have been taken from that meter.\nfunc (qs *queueSet) advanceEpoch(ctx context.Context, now time.Time, incrR fqrequest.SeatSeconds) {\n\toldR := qs.currentR\n\tqs.currentR -= rDecrement\n\tklog.InfoS(\"Advancing epoch\", \"QS\", qs.qCfg.Name, \"when\", now.Format(nsTimeFmt), \n\t\t\"oldR\", oldR, \"newR\", qs.currentR, \"incrR\", incrR)\n\tsuccess := true\n\tfor qIdx, queue := range qs.queues {\n\t\tif queue.requestsWaiting.Length() == 0 && queue.requestsExecuting.Len() == 0 {\n\t\t\t// Safe to reset to zero\n\t\t\tqueue.nextDispatchR = 0\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\t\toldNextDispatchR := \"incrR\", incrR)\n\t\t\t\tsuccess = false\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t})\n\t}\n\tmetrics.AddEpochAdvance(ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, success)\n}\n\n// getVirtualTimeRatio calculates the rate at which virtual time advances\nfunc (qs *queueSet) getVirtualTimeRatioLocked() float64 {\n\tactiveQueues := 0\n\tseatsRequested := 0\n\tfor _, queue := range qs.queues {\n\t\t// sum of max width of requests in this queue for maximum rate\n\t\tseatsRequested += (queue.seatsInUse + queue.requestsWaiting.QueueSum().MaxSeatsSum)\n\t\tif queue.requestsWaiting.Length() > 0 || queue.requestsExecuting.Len() > 0 {\n\t\t\tactiveQueues++\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\tif activeQueues == 0 {\n\t\treturn 0\n\t}\n\treturn math.Min(float64(seatsRequested), float64(qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit)) / float64(activeQueues)\n}\n```\n\n#### dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked - Core Dispatch Loop:\n\n```go\n// dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked does as many dispatches as possible now.\n// This is the main dispatch loop that runs fair queuing.\nfunc (qs *queueSet) dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked() {\n\tfor qs.totRequestsWaiting != 0 && \n\t    qs.totSeatsInUse < qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit && \n\t    qs.dispatchLocked() {\n\t}\n}\n\n// dispatchLocked uses Fair Queuing to select a queue and dispatch the oldest request\nfunc (qs *queueSet) dispatchLocked() bool {\n\tqueue, request := qs.findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()\n\tif queue == nil {\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\tif request == nil { // This should never happen\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\tqs.totRequestsWaiting--\n\tqs.totSeatsWaiting -= -request.MaxSeats())\n\trequest.NoteQueued(false)\n\tqs.reqsGaugePair.RequestsWaiting.Add(-1)\n\tdefer qs.boundNextDispatchLocked(queue)\n\t\n\tif !request.decision.Set(decisionExecute) {\n\t\tqs.seatDemandIntegrator.Set(float64(qs.totSeatsInUse + qs.totSeatsWaiting))\n\t\treturn true\n\t}\n\trequest.startTime = qs.clock.Now()\n\t\n\t// Request leaves queue and starts executing\n\tqs.totRequestsExecuting++\n\tqs.totSeatsInUse += request.MaxSeats()\n\tqueue.requestsExecuting = queue.requestsExecuting.Insert(request)\n\tqueue.seatsInUse += request.MaxSeats()\n\tmetrics.AddRequestsExecuting(request.ctx, qs.qCfg.Name, request.fsName, 1)\n\tmetrics.AddSeatConcurrencyInUse(qs.qCfg.Name, request.fsName, qs.totSeatsWaiting))\n\t\n\tklogV := klog.V(6)\n\tif klogV.Enabled() {\n\t\tklogV.Infof(\"QS(%s) at t=%s R=%v: dispatching request %#+v %#+v work %v from queue %d with start R %v, \"+\n\t\t\t\"queue
