  "content": "# Kubernetes APF QueueSet: Algorithmic Deep-Dive\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies](#1-subsystem-purpose-boundaries-and-dependencies)\n2. [Key Components and Responsibility Split](#2-key-components-and-responsibility-split)\n3. [End-to-End Request Flow](#3-end-to-end-request-flow)\n4. [The Fair Queuing Algorithm in Detail](#4-the-fair-queuing-algorithm-in-detail)\n5. [Concurrency Borrowing and Dynamic Limits](#5-concurrency-borrowing-and-dynamic-limits)\n6. [Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs](#6-failure-modes-limits-and-design-tradeoffs)\n7. [Extension Points and Customization Hooks](#7-extension-points-and-customization-hooks)\n8. [Operational Implications](#8-operational-implications)\n9. [File and Directory Map](#9-file-and-directory-map)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\nAPI Priority and Fairness (APF) is the kube-apiserver's admission control layer for request-level concurrency. Its purpose is to prevent any single actor\u2014user, controller, or client burst\u2014from monopolizing the server while ensuring that critical system traffic (node heartbeats, leader election) is never starved.\n\nThe **QueueSet** is the scheduling unit at the heart of APF. Each non-exempt priority level owns exactly one QueueSet. The QueueSet implements *Fair Queuing for Server Requests* (FQSR), a variant of weighted fair queuing adapted to multi-seat, multi-phase request processing.\n\n### Boundaries\n\n**APF sits between the HTTP router and the actual handler chain.** It is invoked as an `Interface.Handle()` call inside the apiserver's filter stack, after authentication and authorization but before the request reaches storage.\n\n```\n[Client HTTP] \u2192 [Authn] \u2192 [Authz] \u2192 [APF Handle()] \u2192 [Handler/Storage]\n```\n\nAPF itself does not parse request bodies or interact with etcd. Its outputs are:\n\n- **Execute** the request \u2014 calls the `execFn` closure passed by the caller.\n- **Reject** the request \u2014 returns without calling `execFn`.\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n\n| Dependency | Role |\n|---|---|\n| `k8s.io/api/flowcontrol/v1` | API types: `FlowSchema`, `PriorityLevelConfiguration` |\n| `k8s.io/client-go/informers` | Watches for config object changes |\n| `k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/request` | `RequestInfo` and user info from context |\n| `k8s.io/utils/clock` | Monotonic time for virtual-time tracking |\n\n### Downstream Dependencies\n\n| Downstream | What APF provides |\n|---|---|\n| kube-apiserver handler chain | Admission gate: calls or skips `execFn` |\n| Prometheus metrics | Per-priority-level concurrency, seat usage, queue depth, wait time |\n\n### Configuration Objects\n\nTwo CRD-like API objects configure APF at runtime:\n\n- **`FlowSchema`** \u2014 classifies incoming requests to a priority level and extracts a *flow distinguisher* (the key that determines which queue within a priority level a request lands in).\n- **`PriorityLevelConfiguration`** \u2014 defines a priority level's concurrency shares, lendable fraction, and queuing parameters (number of queues, hand size, queue length limit).\n\nThese live in `k8s.io/api/flowcontrol/v1` and their internal representation is in `pkg/apis/flowcontrol/types.go`.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 `Interface` and `configController`\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_filter.go`\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go`\n\n`configController` implements the `Interface` interface and is the top-level object instantiated by the apiserver. It has two concurrent duties:\n\n1. **Config reconciliation worker** (`runWorker` goroutine): watches FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration objects via informers. Any change enqueues token `0` into `configQueue`. The worker reads all objects, creates or updates `priorityLevelState` entries, and calls `QueueSet.BeginConfigChange` / `.Complete` to push new parameters down.\n\n2. **Borrowing rebalancer** (`updateBorrowing` goroutine): fires every 10 seconds (`borrowingAdjustmentPeriod`). It reads seat demand statistics accumulated in each priority level's `seatDemandIntegrator`, applies smoothing, and recomputes `currentCL` (the *dynamic* concurrency limit) for each level.\n\n`configController` holds:\n- `flowSchemas` \u2014 sorted slice of all active `FlowSchema` objects, ordered by ascending `MatchingPrecedence` (lower number = higher priority).\n- `priorityLevelStates` \u2014 map from priority-level name to `priorityLevelState`, which carries the `QueueSet`, demand statistics, and concurrency bounds.\n\n### 2.2 `priorityLevelState`\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go:201`\n\nPer-priority-level bookkeeping:\n\n```go\ntype priorityLevelState struct {\n    pl            *flowcontrol.PriorityLevelConfiguration\n    qsCompleter   fq.QueueSetCompleter\n    queues        fq.QueueSet          // the live QueueSet\n    quiescing     bool                 // draining, to be removed when empty\n    nominalCL     int                  // configured concurrency shares\n    minCL         int                  // nominalCL - lendable\n    maxCL         int                  // nominalCL + borrowable\n    currentCL     int                  // dynamic limit, set every 10s\n    seatDemandIntegrator fq.Integrator // time-weighted seat demand accumulator\n    seatDemandStats seatDemandStats    // statistics derived from integrator\n}\n```\n\nThe three concurrency bounds come from the API object fields `NominalConcurrencyShares` and `LendablePercent`:\n- `minCL = nominalCL * (1 - LendablePercent/100)` \u2014 seats that cannot be borrowed away\n- `maxCL = nominalCL + (sum of other levels' lendable)` \u2014 seats that can be borrowed in\n\n### 2.3 `QueueSet` and `queueSet`\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/interface.go`\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go`\n\n`QueueSet` is the public interface. `queueSet` is its concrete implementation. One instance exists per non-exempt priority level. It owns:\n\n- A slice of `*queue` objects (one per virtual queue)\n- The progress meter `currentR` (virtual time, in seat-seconds)\n- `dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit` \u2014 the limit currently enforced (equals `currentCL` from the controller)\n- `dealer` \u2014 the shuffle sharding dealer used for queue selection\n\nThe `QueueSet` interface has four methods:\n- `BeginConfigChange(QueuingConfig) (QueueSetCompleter, error)` \u2014 phase 1 of reconfiguration; validates and prepares\n- `Complete(DispatchingConfig) QueueSet` \u2014 phase 2; applies the new concurrency limit\n- `StartRequest(...)` (req, idle)` \u2014 enqueues or immediately dispatches a new request\n- `Dump(includeRequestDetails bool)` \u2014 debug snapshot, stops admission briefly\n\n### 2.4 `queue`\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go:92`\n\nA single virtual queue within a QueueSet:\n\n```go\ntype queue struct {\n    requestsWaiting   fifo               // FIFO list of waiting requests\n    nextDispatchR     fcrequest.SeatSeconds // virtual time of next dispatch\n    requestsExecuting sets.Set[*request]  // currently running requests\n    index             int                 // position in qs.queues\n    seatsInUse        int                 // seats held by executing requests\n}\n```\n\n`nextDispatchR` is the key field for fairness. The dispatch algorithm selects the queue whose `nextDispatchR + oldestRequest.totalWork()` is smallest \u2014 that is, the queue with the smallest *virtual finish time* for its next request.\n\n### 2.5 `request`\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go:33`\n\nA wrapper around a single in-flight or waiting request:\n\n```go\ntype request struct {\n    ctx              context.Context\n    qs               *queueSet\n    queue            *queue           // nil if exempt/no-queue path\n    workEstimate     completedWorkEstimate\n    decision         promise.WriteOnce  // set once: execute or cancel\n    arrivalTime      time.Time\n    arrivalR         fcrequest.SeatSeconds  // qs.currentR at arrival\n    startTime        time.Time\n    removeFromQueueLocked removeFromFIFOFunc\n}\n```\n\nThe `decision` field is a `WriteOnce` promise. Exactly one goroutine will call `decision.Set(decisionExecute)` or `decision.Set(decisionCancel)`. The goroutine waiting in `request.wait()` blocks on `decision.Get()`.\n\n### 2.6 `completedWorkEstimate` and Work Estimation\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/width.go`\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go:85`\n\nWork is measured in *seat-seconds*: the product of concurrency seats occupied and time. The `WorkEstimate` has three fields:\n\n```go\ntype WorkEstimate struct {\n    InitialSeats     uint64        // seats during main execution\n    FinalSeats       uint64        // seats during post-execution cleanup\n    AdditionalLatency time.Duration // duration of cleanup phase\n}\n```\n\nThese are lifted into `completedWorkEstimate` by pre-computing `totalWork` and `finalWork` at enqueue time using the QueueSet's `estimatedServiceDuration` (hardcoded to 3ms):\n\n```go\ninitialWork = SeatsTimesDuration(InitialSeats, estimatedServiceDuration)\nfinalWork   = SeatsTimesDuration(FinalSeats,   AdditionalLatency)\ntotalWork   = initialWork + finalWork\n```\n\n`totalWork` is what `nextDispatchR` advances by after each dispatch, making it the fairness currency.\n\nThe `workEstimator` (in `request/width.go`) maps HTTP verb to seat count:\n- `list` / `watch` \u2192 `listWorkEstimator`: scales seats with estimated object count\n- `create`, `update`, `patch`, `delete` \u2192 `mutatingWorkEstimator`: scales with active watch count\n- all others \u2192 `minimumSeats` (1 seat)\n\n### 2.7 Shuffle Sharding Dealer\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go`\n\nThe `Dealer` maps a `uint64` hash to a \"hand\" of queue indices using a Fisher-Yates-inspired shuffle. Given `deckSize` (number of queues) and `handSize`, it deals `handSize` distinct cards:\n\n```go\nfunc (d *Dealer) Deal(hashValue uint64, pick func(int)) {\n    var remainders [15]int\n    for i := 0; i < d.handSize; i++ {\n        hashValueNext := hashValue / uint64(d.deckSize-i)\n        remainders[i] = int(hashValue - uint64(d.deckSize-i)*hashValueNext)\n        hashValue = hashValueNext\n    }\n    for i := 0; i < d.handSize; i++ {\n        card := remainders[i]\n        for j := i; j > 0; j-- {\n            if card >= remainders[j-1] { card++ }\n        }\n        pick(card)\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThe hand is dealt from the hash without replacement, so the `handSize` indices are distinct. This provides isolation: two flows that share hash collisions can share at most `handSize` queues, reducing the probability of starvation through collision to an astronomically small value.\n\n### 2.8 `WriteOnce` Promise\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/promise/promise.go`\n\n```go\ntype promise struct {\n    doneCtx context.Context\n    doneVal interface{}\n    setCh   chan struct{}\n    onceler sync.Once\n    value   interface{}\n}\n```\n\n`Set` uses `sync.Once` to guarantee single-write semantics and closes `setCh` to unblock `Get`. `Get` selects on `setCh` or `doneCtx.Done()`, which acts as a deadline/cancellation hook. If the context is cancelled before a dispatch decision, `Get` calls `Set(doneVal)` \u2014 in practice `decisionCancel` \u2014 so the waiting goroutine wakes and cleans up.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow\n\nThe flow has five distinct phases.\n\n### Phase 1: Classification (`Handle` \u2192 `startRequest`)\n\n`configController.Handle` is invoked by the apiserver filter for every non-exempt-by-bypass request. It calls `startRequest`, which:\n\n1. **Acquires a read lock** on `cfgCtlr.lock`.\n2. **Iterates `flowSchemas`** in order of ascending `MatchingPrecedence`. For each schema, it tests the request's user and resource against the schema's `Rules`. The first match wins.\n3. **Extracts the flow distinguisher**: either the user's name (ByUser), the resource namespace (ByNamespace), or empty string (no distinguishing).\n4. **Hashes** the flow distinguisher with `crypto/sha256` and takes the first 8 bytes as a `uint64`.\n5. **Calls `noteFn`** with the matched FlowSchema and PriorityLevelConfiguration \u2014 this is the hook for the caller to record classification results.\n6. **Calls `workEstimator`** (only for non-exempt levels) to get the `WorkEstimate`.\n7. **Calls `plState.queues.StartRequest(...)`** on the priority level's QueueSet.\n\n```\nHandle(ctx, requestDigest, noteFn, workEstimator, queueNoteFn, execFn)\n  \u2514\u2500 startRequest(...)\n       \u251c\u2500 match FlowSchema (sorted by precedence)\n       \u251c\u2500 extract flow distinguisher\n       \u251c\u2500 SHA256 hash \u2192 uint64\n       \u251c\u2500 workEstimator() \u2192 WorkEstimate\n       \u2514\u2500 plState.queues.StartRequest(ctx, &workEstimate, hashValue, ...)\n```\n\n### Phase 2: Queue Assignment (`StartRequest`)\n\n`queueSet.StartRequest` acquires `qs.lock` and immediately calls `syncTimeLocked` to advance virtual time before touching any queue state.\n\n**No-queues path** (`DesiredNumQueues < 1`):\n\nIf the priority level has no queues (either exempt or configured as zero-queue), the request is immediately dispatched if `totSeatsInUse + MaxSeats <= ConcurrencyLimit`, or rejected otherwise. The decision promise is pre-set to `decisionExecute`.\n\n**Queues path** (`DesiredNumQueues > 0`):\n\n1. **Shuffle shard**: `shuffleShardLocked` calls `dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, ...)` to get `handSize` queue indices. It then picks the queue with the minimum `TotalWorkSum` (total seat-seconds of waiting requests). Ties are broken by the rotation offset `qs.enqueues % handSize` \u2014 cycling through tied queues prevents pathological convergence.\n\n2. **Reject or enqueue**: `rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked` checks whether the chosen queue is full *and* the QueueSet is at its concurrency limit. If both conditions hold, the request is rejected with reason `\"queue-full\"`. Otherwise the request is added to the queue's FIFO (`enqueueToBoundLocked`).\n\n   When enqueuing to an empty queue, `nextDispatchR` is initialized to `qs.currentR`, giving the newly active queue a fresh start in virtual time.\n\n3. **`dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked`** runs the dispatch loop before returning.\n\n4. `StartRequest` returns the `*request` object. The caller (the filter layer) gets a non-nil `fq.Request`.\n\n### Phase 3: Dispatch Loop (`dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked`)\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked() {\n    for qs.totRequestsWaiting != 0 &&\n        qs.totSeatsInUse < qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit &&\n        qs.dispatchLocked() {\n    }\n}\n```\n\nEach call to `dispatchLocked`:\n\n1. Calls `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked` to select the queue and oldest request.\n2. Dequeues the request (`removeFromQueueLocked`).\n3. Calls `request.decision.Set(decisionExecute)`.\n4. Moves the request from `queue.requestsWaiting` to `queue.requestsExecuting`.\n5. Increments seat counters.\n6. Updates `queue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()` \u2014 advancing this queue's virtual time by the request's work.\n7. Calls `boundNextDispatchLocked(queue)` (anti-windup, explained below).\n\nIf `canAccommodateSeatsLocked` returns false (the head request needs more seats than currently available), `dispatchLocked` returns false and the loop stops. This can happen when a wide request (many seats) is at the head but other executing requests have not yet freed their seats.\n\n### Phase 4: Waiting for Decision (`Request.Finish`)\n\nBack in the caller (`Handle`), `req.Finish(execFn)` is called. This:\n\n1. Calls `req.wait()`, which calls `req.decision.Get()`. This **blocks** until either the dispatch loop sets `decisionExecute` or the request's context is cancelled (which triggers `decisionCancel` via the promise's `doneCtx`).\n\n2. On `decisionExecute`: records queue wait time metrics, calls `execFn()`, then calls `finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible`.\n\n3. On `decisionCancel` (context timeout or explicit cancellation):\n   - If the request is still in the queue, `removeFromQueueLocked` removes it.\n   - Counters are decremented, metrics record a `\"time-out\"` reject.\n   - `boundNextDispatchLocked` is called so the anti-windup invariant is maintained.\n   - Returns without calling `execFn`.\n\n### Phase 5: Request Completion (`finishRequestLocked`)\n\nAfter `execFn()` returns:\n\n1. `totRequestsExecuting--`, seat counters decremented.\n2. **Service time correction**: `queue.nextDispatchR` is *adjusted backwards* by the difference between estimated and actual service time:\n   ```\n   queue.nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration(InitialSeats, estimatedServiceDuration - actualServiceDuration)\n   ```\n   If the request finished faster than estimated, the queue's virtual time is wound back \u2014 rewarding fast requests by allowing the queue to dispatch sooner next cycle.\n\n3. **Two-phase seats** (`AdditionalLatency > 0`): If the work estimate has cleanup work (`FinalSeats` > 0 and `AdditionalLatency` > 0), seats are *not* released immediately. `clock.EventAfterDuration(releaseSeatsLocked, AdditionalLatency)` schedules a callback. This models write-back work (e.g., updating the apiserver's watch cache after a mutation) that occupies seats but does not block the HTTP response.\n\n4. `boundNextDispatchLocked` is applied.\n5. `dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked` runs again to fill freed capacity.\n\n---\n\n## 4. The Fair Queuing Algorithm in Detail\n\n### 4.1 Virtual Time (`currentR`)\n\nThe progress meter `currentR` is a global `SeatSeconds` value shared across all queues in a QueueSet. It tracks \"how much work has been allocated per queue\" and advances at a rate proportional to utilization.\n\n`syncTimeLocked` is called every time the lock is acquired:\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) syncTimeLocked(ctx context.Context) {\n    realNow := qs.clock.Now()\n    timeSinceLast := realNow.Sub(qs.lastRealTime)\n    qs.lastRealTime = realNow\n    incrR := SeatsTimesDuration(qs.getVirtualTimeRatioLocked(), timeSinceLast)\n    qs.currentR = prevR + incrR\n    // ... epoch advance if needed\n}\n```\n\nThe rate `getVirtualTimeRatioLocked()` is:\n\n```\nrate = min(totalSeatsRequested, ConcurrencyLimit) / activeQueues\n```\n\nWhere `totalSeatsRequested = sum over all queues of (seatsInUse + MaxSeatsSum of waiting requests)` and `activeQueues` is the count of non-empty queues. When all queues are empty, `rate = 0` and virtual time stops.\n\nThis formulation means: virtual time advances by `ConcurrencyLimit / activeQueues` seat-seconds per real second when the system is fully loaded, or less when underloaded.\n\n### 4.2 Queue Selection (`findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked`)\n\nThe dispatch algorithm is WF\u00b2Q+ (Worst-case Fair Weighted Fair Queuing, Squared):\n\n```\nFor each non-empty queue:\n    virtualFinish = queue.nextDispatchR + oldestRequest.totalWork()\n\nSelect the queue with minimum virtualFinish.\n```\n\nThe round-robin scan (`robinIndex`) ensures that among queues with equal virtual finish times, the tie is broken fairly rather than always favouring the same queue.\n\nAfter selecting, `qs.robinIndex = minIndex` \u2014 the next scan starts at the selected queue's successor, preventing it from winning ties in consecutive rounds.\n\n```go\nfor range qs.queues {\n    qs.robinIndex = (qs.robinIndex + 1) % nq\n    queue := qs.queues[qs.robinIndex]\n    oldestWaiting, _ := queue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\n    if oldestWaiting != nil {\n        currentVirtualFinish := queue.nextDispatchR + oldestWaiting.totalWork()\n        if currentVirtualFinish < minVirtualFinish {\n            minVirtualFinish = currentVirtualFinish\n            minQueue = queue\n            minIndex = qs.robinIndex\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nAfter dispatch, `nextDispatchR` advances:\n```go\nqueue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()\n```\n\nThis charges the queue for the work it just dispatched: a queue that sends many large requests falls behind queues sending small ones.\n\n### 4.3 Anti-Windup (`boundNextDispatchLocked`)\n\nA queue that is slow to use its allocation (e.g., its flow produces requests infrequently) will accumulate credit as `nextDispatchR` falls behind `currentR`. When such a queue does produce a burst, it would get unfairly preferential treatment because its `nextDispatchR + work` is very small.\n\nThe anti-windup hack prevents `nextDispatchR` from falling below the `arrivalR` of the queue's oldest waiting request:\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) boundNextDispatchLocked(queue *queue) {\n    oldestReq, _ := queue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\n    if oldestReq == nil { return }\n    if queue.nextDispatchR < oldestReq.arrivalR {\n        queue.nextDispatchR = oldestReq.arrivalR\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis is called after every dispatch and after every enqueue. The comment in the code explicitly labels this a \"hack\" \u2014 the ideal solution would assign each queue exactly the seats it can use, but that is computationally expensive and the bound is a practical approximation.\n\n### 4.4 Service Time Correction\n\nWhen a request finishes, the QueueSet corrects `nextDispatchR` for the difference between estimated and actual service:\n\n```go\nr.queue.nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration(\n    float64(r.InitialSeats()),\n    qs.estimatedServiceDuration - actualServiceDuration,\n)\n```\n\nIf `actualServiceDuration < estimatedServiceDuration`, the subtraction is positive (nextDispatchR decreases), giving the queue credit back. If the request took longer than estimated, `nextDispatchR` increases, penalising the queue. This makes the algorithm self-calibrating over time.\n\n### 4.5 Epoch Advancement (Overflow Prevention)\n\n`currentR` is a `SeatSeconds` value backed by a fixed-size integer type. To prevent overflow, when `currentR >= highR`, all virtual time readings are uniformly decremented by `rDecrement`:\n\n```go\nconst rDecrement = fqrequest.MaxSeatSeconds / 2\nconst highR = rDecrement + rDecrement/2\n\nfunc (qs *queueSet) advanceEpoch(ctx context.Context, now time.Time, incrR fqrequest.SeatSeconds) {\n    qs.currentR -= rDecrement\n    for _, queue := range qs.queues {\n        if queue.requestsWaiting.Length() == 0 && queue.requestsExecuting.Len() == 0 {\n            queue.nextDispatchR = 0  // safe reset for idle queues\n            continue\n        }\n        queue.nextDispatchR -= rDecrement\n        queue.requestsWaiting.Walk(func(req *request) bool {\n            req.arrivalR -= rDecrement\n            return true\n        })\n    }\n}\n```\n\nEmpty queues are reset to zero rather than decremented, since their `nextDispatchR` will be overwritten when the next request arrives. The metric `apiserver_flowcontrol_epoch_advance_total` tracks epoch advances.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Concurrency Borrowing and Dynamic Limits\n\n### 5.1 Motivation\n\nStatic concurrency shares result in wasted capacity: a level configured for 40 seats but receiving only 5 rps of traffic leaves 35 seats idle, while an overloaded level is constrained to its nominal allocation. Borrowing allows idle capacity to be redistributed dynamically.\n\n### 5.2 Seat Demand Measurement\n\nEach priority level carries a `seatDemandIntegrator` (a time-weighted integrator). Every time a request is enqueued or finishes execution, the integrator is updated:\n\n```go\nqs.seatDemandIntegrator.Set(float64(qs.totSeatsInUse + qs.totSeatsWaiting))\n```\n\nEvery 10 seconds, the borrowing loop calls `integrator.Reset()`, which returns `IntegratorResults` containing `Average`, `Deviation` (standard deviation), `Max`, and `Duration`. These statistics describe the demand distribution over the last adjustment period.\n\n### 5.3 Smoothing\n\nRaw demand is volatile. A single burst should not permanently award seats to a level, nor should a momentary lull cause seats to be taken away. The `seatDemandStats.update` method applies exponential smoothing:\n\n```go\nenvelope := obs.Average + obs.Deviation  // \"envelope\" = avg + 1 stdDev\n\nstats.smoothed = math.Max(envelope,\n    seatDemandSmoothingCoefficient*stats.smoothed +\n    (1-seatDemandSmoothingCoefficient)*envelope)\n```\n\nThe coefficient `0.977` is chosen so the half-life of the smoothed value is approximately 5 minutes. The `math.Max` ensures smoothed never drops faster than one time constant \u2014 it tracks peaks more aggressively than valleys.\n\n### 5.4 Allocation (`updateBorrowingLocked`)\n\nEvery 10 seconds, `updateBorrowingLocked` runs the allocation algorithm:\n\n1. **Exempt levels** are served first: their `currentCL` is set to `max(minCL, highWatermark)`. Their allocation is subtracted from `remainingServerCL`.\n\n2. For non-exempt levels, each level is assigned:\n   - `lowerBound = max(minCL, min(nominalCL, highWatermark))`\n   - `upperBound = maxCL`\n   - `target = max(lowerBound, smoothed)`\n\n3. `computeConcurrencyAllocation` solves a proportional allocation problem: given the remaining server capacity and the per-level (lowerBound, upperBound, target), distribute seats to minimise the sum of squared fractional shortfalls. Levels at their lower bound consume less; levels at their target receive their smoothed demand; no level exceeds its upper bound.\n\n4. The result is rounded to an integer and passed as `ConcurrencyLimit` to `QueueSet.Complete(DispatchingConfig{ConcurrencyLimit: currentCL})`, which takes effect immediately.\n\nThere are three degenerate cases:\n- `remainingServerCL <= minCLSum`: every level falls to its minimum.\n- `minCLSum < remainingServerCL <= minCurrentCLSum`: a proportional share `shareFrac` is applied between minimum and observed demand.\n- `remainingServerCL > minCurrentCLSum`: full proportional allocation runs.\n\n### 5.5 Operational Consequence\n\nDynamic borrowing means that `currentCL` can differ substantially from `nominalCL` during traffic surges. A level might temporarily receive double its nominal seats if other levels are idle, then lose them within one adjustment period. Operators should monitor `apiserver_flowcontrol_current_limit_seats` alongside `apiserver_flowcontrol_nominal_limit_seats` to understand actual enforcement.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 6.1 Wide Request Blocking\n\nIf the head-of-queue request needs `N` seats and only `N-1` are available, the dispatch loop stops entirely for that queue, even if other requests behind it need only 1 seat. The `canAccommodateSeatsLocked` code does have an escape hatch: if `totRequestsExecuting == 0` but the request needs more seats than `ConcurrencyLimit`, it is dispatched anyway (HOL-blocking is unavoidable when the request genuinely exceeds total capacity). Outside that case, the system waits.\n\nThis is head-of-line (HOL) blocking in the virtual world. Wide requests (e.g., LIST on a huge object type) can temporarily block narrow requests in the same queue. Because shuffle sharding distributes flows across queues, the blast radius is limited to flows sharing queue indices with the wide request.\n\n### 6.2 Queue Full Rejection\n\nRejection reason `\"queue-full\"` occurs when `totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit` AND the chosen queue has reached `QueueLengthLimit`. This is the intentional shedding point. Under overload, well-configured systems should shed load here rather than allowing infinite queue growth and timeouts.\n\nOperators can tune `QueueLengthLimit` and the number of queues to control memory footprint versus rejection rate tradeoff.\n\n### 6.3 Anti-Windup Approximation\n\nThe `boundNextDispatchLocked` hack prevents credit accumulation but does not perfectly model fair share allocation. A queue that does not use its allocation should, in theory, be penalised relative to queues that do. The current scheme neither penalises nor credits: it simply prevents the windfall of accumulated credit. This is acknowledged in the code comments as a known approximation.\n\n### 6.4 Estimated Service Duration\n\n`estimatedServiceDuration` is hardcoded to `3 * time.Millisecond` (`queueset.go:215`). This constant directly scales `initialWork = InitialSeats * estimatedServiceDuration`, which is the primary fairness currency. If actual requests are systematically much faster or slower than 3ms, the virtual work estimates will be off, but the service-time correction in `finishRequestLocked` self-calibrates `nextDispatchR` over time. The hardcoded value is most critical at startup, before corrections have accumulated.\n\n### 6.5 Borrowing Lag\n\nConcurrency limits are adjusted only every 10 seconds. A sudden burst that depletes a level's allocation in under 10 seconds must wait for the next rebalance. The smoothing coefficient further slows adaptation \u2014 a single 10-second spike contributes only ~2.3% to the smoothed value. This conservative tuning avoids thrashing but means overload recovery is measured in minutes.\n\n### 6.6 Epoch Advance Atomicity\n\n`advanceEpoch` iterates all queues and all waiting requests to subtract `rDecrement`. With thousands of queues and deep queues, this is an O(queues \u00d7 depth) operation under lock. During this time, all other admission is blocked. In practice, the number of queues per priority level is bounded by the configured `DesiredNumQueues` (typically 64\u2013128), and queue depth is bounded by `QueueLengthLimit`, so the operation is bounded. However, operators should not configure unusually large values.\n\n### 6.7 Configuration Consistency\n\nBecause APF configuration is reconciled from API objects, there is an inherent lag between operator intent and enforced policy. The controller processes changes via an informer and a rate-limited work queue. During the reconciliation window, old policy is in effect. The mandatory `exempt` and `catch-all` FlowSchemas and PriorityLevelConfigurations are bootstrapped at startup and cannot be deleted, providing a safety floor.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 7.1 `QueueSetFactory`\n\nThe `QueueSetFactory` interface (`fairqueuing/interface.go:32`) is a dependency-injection point. The apiserver passes `fqs.NewQueueSetFactory(clk)` in production, but tests substitute a `newTestableQueueSetFactory` that injects a fake event clock and a custom `promiseFactoryFactory`. This allows deterministic replay of dispatch sequences in tests without real time passing.\n\nAny component embedding APF can provide an alternative `QueueSetFactory` to use a different queuing discipline, provided it satisfies the interface. The interface contract is tight (two-phase construction, StartRequest semantics), so alternative implementations must be careful to maintain virtual-time semantics if they want borrowing to function correctly.\n\n### 7.2 `WorkEstimatorFunc`\n\n`WorkEstimatorFunc` (`request/width.go:89`) is the pluggable work estimation function. The default estimates are based on object counts (for list) and watch counts (for mutations). Operators cannot change this at runtime, but API server builds can substitute a custom `WorkEstimatorFunc` at construction time.\n\nThe returned `WorkEstimate` directly controls how many seats a request occupies and for how long. An incorrect estimate (too high) reduces throughput; too low allows requests to under-contribute to fairness accounting.\n\n### 7.3 `noteFn` and `queueNoteFn`\n\nThe `Handle` signature accepts two callbacks:\n- `noteFn(fs, pl, flowDistinguisher)` \u2014 called immediately after classification, before queuing. Used by the caller (kube-apiserver's filter layer) to attach request metadata to logs and metrics.\n- `queueNoteFn(inQueue bool)` \u2014 called when a request enters and leaves a queue. Used by the dropped-requests tracker (`dropped_requests_tracker.go`) to detect and surface requests that are spending excessive time queued.\n\nThese hooks have no effect on scheduling decisions. They are safe to implement with side effects (metrics, logs) but must not block.\n\n### 7.4 Bootstrap Defaults\n\n`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/apis/flowcontrol/bootstrap/default.go` defines the mandatory and suggested FlowSchemas and PriorityLevelConfigurations. Operators cannot change the mandatory objects but can override or supplement the suggested ones. Any customisation that removes the `catch-all` or `exempt` objects risks breaking the cluster.\n\nSuggested levels (`workload-high`, `workload-low`, `global-default`, `leader-election`, `node-high`, `system`) represent Kubernetes's reference allocation. They can be tuned via `NominalConcurrencyShares` and `LendablePercent` without code changes.\n\n### 7.5 `MaxSeatsTracker`\n\n`configController` also implements `MaxSeatsTracker`, which caps the maximum seats the work estimator may assign to a request for a given priority level. The constant `priorityLevelMaxSeatsPercent = 0.15` (`apf_controller.go:63`) means the cap is set at 15% of `nominalCL`, preventing a single request from claiming more than a fraction of a priority level's capacity. This cap is passed into `NewWorkEstimator` as `maxSeatsFn` and enforced in the list and mutating estimators.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Operational Implications\n\n### 8.1 Metrics for Day-to-Day Operations\n\nThe most operationally relevant metrics are:\n\n| Metric | Meaning |\n|---|---|\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_current_inqueue_requests` | Queue depth per level and flow schema |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_current_executing_requests` | In-flight requests per level |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_current_limit_seats` | The dynamic `currentCL` (post-borrowing) |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_nominal_limit_seats` | The static `nominalCL` |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_request_wait_duration_seconds` | Time requests spend in queue |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_rejected_requests_total` | Rejections by reason (`queue-full`, `concurrency-limit`, `time-out`) |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_demand_seats` | Smoothed seat demand used for borrowing decisions |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_dispatch_r` | Current virtual time (for debugging virtual-world state) |\n\nSustained `queue-full` rejections indicate that a priority level is underprovisioned relative to its request rate. Sustained `time-out` rejections indicate requests are waiting longer than their context deadline allows \u2014 often a sign of a concurrency cliff where many slow requests monopolise seats.\n\n### 8.2 Two-Phase Seat Holding and Watch Mutations\n\nThe `AdditionalLatency` / `FinalSeats` model deserves particular attention. Mutating requests (create, update, delete) trigger fan-out to watch clients. The `mutatingWorkEstimator` uses the watch count to estimate `FinalSeats` and `AdditionalLatency`, causing the request to hold seats after the HTTP response has been sent. This back-pressure mechanism prevents watch fan-out from drowning the apiserver's internal work queue.\n\nOperators observing high `execSeats` gauge values after low `executingRequests` values may be seeing requests in their final phase. Tuning `AdditionalLatency` heuristics requires understanding the watch count distribution of the cluster.\n\n### 8.3 Queue Count and Hand Size Trade-offs\n\nMore queues reduce hash collision probability (isolation between flows) but increase per-lock iteration cost in `findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked` (O(numQueues) per dispatch). Larger hand size improves load balancing within the set of queues a flow can land in but consumes more hash entropy and increases scan time during queue selection.\n\nThe default of 128 queues, hand size 6 provides collision probability of approximately `(6/128)^2 \u2248 0.22%` for any two flows to share all their queues \u2014 meaning even a malicious or runaway flow can only monopolise a tiny fraction of queue slots.\n\n### 8.4 Priority Level Lifecycle and Quiescing\n\nWhen a PriorityLevelConfiguration is deleted or the `DesiredNumQueues` drops to zero, the corresponding queues are not immediately removed. Instead, `quiescing` is set to true and queues drain naturally. The `removeQueueIfEmptyLocked` function removes individual queues as they become idle. Only when all queues are empty and `quiescing` is true is the priority level state fully removed.\n\nThis graceful drainage prevents in-flight requests from being disrupted during config rollouts. Operators rolling out APF configuration changes should account for the drain time \u2014 requests can take up to `context.Timeout` to complete, plus any `AdditionalLatency`.\n\n### 8.5 Lock Contention\n\nThe QueueSet uses a single `sync.Mutex` for all state. Every admission decision (`StartRequest`) and every completion (`Finish`) acquires this lock. Under high request rates (thousands of RPS per priority level), this lock can become a bottleneck. Each critical section is short \u2014 typically a few microseconds \u2014 but the cumulative effect at high load merits attention.\n\nThe design choice of one lock per QueueSet rather than per-queue locking is intentional: the virtual time and cross-queue dispatch logic would require complex fine-grained locking to preserve correctness. The single lock also makes the dispatch logic easier to reason about and test.\n\n### 8.6 Maintainability: Two-Phase Configuration\n\nThe `BeginConfigChange` / `Complete` two-phase update pattern exists to separate config validation (which can return errors) from application (which cannot fail). This makes it safe to validate new configuration before committing to it, and allows the controller to fall back gracefully if a new config is invalid. Any code extending the configuration protocol must preserve this separation.\n\n---\n\n## 9. File and Directory Map\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 apf_filter.go           Interface definition; Handle() entry point; New() constructor\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 apf_controller.go       configController; priorityLevelState; updateBorrowing; startRequest\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 apf_controller_debug.go Debug endpoint for /debug/api_priority_and_fairness/dump_priority_levels\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 apf_context.go          Context key types for APF request metadata\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 conc_alloc.go           computeConcurrencyAllocation: solves proportional allocation LP\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 dropped_requests_tracker.go Tracks requests spending too long in queue\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 max_seats.go            MaxSeatsTracker interface and implementation\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 watch_tracker.go        WatchTracker: counts active watches per resource, feeds mutating estimator\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 fairqueuing/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 interface.go        QueueSet, QueueSetFactory, Request, QueuingConfig, DispatchingConfig\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 integrator.go       Integrator: time-weighted average/stddev/max accumulator\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 eventclock/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 interface.go    Interface wrapping time.Now and EventAfterDuration\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 real.go         Production clock implementation\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 promise/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 interface.go    WriteOnce interface\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 promise.go      Thread-safe single-write promise with context cancellation\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 queueset/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 queueset.go     FQSR implementation: StartRequest, dispatchLocked, syncTimeLocked,\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2502                   shuffleShardLocked, finishRequestLocked, boundNextDispatchLocked\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 types.go        request, queue, queueSum, completedWorkEstimate type definitions\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 fifo_list.go    FIFO list with O(1) removal;
